Discussion Title: Should high-income countries take in refugees?

1. High-income countries should take in significant numbers of refugees.
1.1. Pro: Closing borders to refugees is equivalent to committing an act of violence against those refugees. It is not an omission - a failure to help someone in need - but an active harm.
1.1.1. Con: Border controls may be an act of "moral omission," but they cannot be inherently considered "acts of violence/harm," since such a designation applies only when one's rights or wellbeing are directly infringed/harmed, and people do not have a right to migrate.
1.1.1.1. Pro: As an illustration of distinction between moral omission and act of harm: Preventing a homeless person from sleeping in one's house is not actively "harming" them. The homeless person would likely be no worse off if the owner hadn't built/maintained their house. It might be moral to let the homeless person in but that person does not have a negative right to gain access to the house, which is the key definition/claim in [Enforcing border...](https://www.kialo.com/argument/2214.105).
1.1.1.1.1. Con: The analogy of building a house does not necessarily compare to state-based land ownership and exclusion. Particularly, a state's control over land is not *created* property like someone who builds and maintains a house "creates" property; a state's control over land is \(usually\) derived from force or threat of force.
1.1.1.2. Con: States should not inherently be able to claim and exclude others from land through force.
The concept of a nation-state exclusively "owning" land is immoral because it did not "create" the land in the sense that a person "creates" a house. States exert their dominance over others through sheer force, which does not result in a just determination of land ownership.
1.1.1.2.1. Con: It is true that the state did not "create" the land, but so long as it does maintain it through force/exclusion, it has a [negative right](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negative_and_positive_rights) \(according to [libertarian conceptions](https://www.libertarianism.org/media/around-web/positive-rights-vs-negative-rights)\) to sovereignty over that property. This may or may not be "intuitively just" or "utilitarian" but based on a negative right approach - as seemingly adopted by \([Enforcing border controls...](https://www.kialo.com/argument/2214.105)\) - this territory belongs to the sovereignty of the country.
1.1.1.2.2. Con: Morality doesn't exist before basic principles.  Unless property is held through force by a government of laws farming, homes and civilization is not possible.
1.1.1.2.2.1. Con: This discussion is about a moral question and the meaning of the elements of the discussion are assumed.    Your question is off topic because it is at a deeper level of analysis than the issue at hand.  My ideas about meaning are based on Wittgenstein's Blue Book and my ideas about a level of analysis are based on Wittgenstein's Tractatus.
1.1.1.2.2.2. Con: Often we hear arguments based on disbelief. Belief and disbelief are unverifiable opinions and undermine the idea of a discussion based on logic. One can disagree with facts in an argument but that disagreement should be well formed and be based on give a different set of facts that contradict the one used in the initial argument.
1.1.1.2.2.3. Con: If all property is based on theft then property is an immoral act akin to murder or rape. No moral act can based on an immoral one. Therefore it is immoral to help someone with stolen goods.
1.1.1.2.3. Con: Ownership is determined by force. A state owns a land if and only if the state can defend the land. A "state" is created by a large enough group of people banding together and agreeing to defend group ownership of a land aka. "sovereignty". This is not to say that ownership should be determined by force but rather acknowledgment that ownership is determined by force.
1.1.2. Pro: If we simply did nothing, refugees would be able to voluntarily enter our countries. Preventing them from doing so requires actively using the threat of violence to stop them from accessing our countries. This is an active harm.
1.1.2.1. Con: This is an unreasonable standard, as it would deny any form of territorial control. For example, one could not prevent anyone from using a private road without paying the toll, as that would require the use of force.
1.1.2.1.1. Con: This is not an appropriate analogy, as typically people are not in desperate need of using private roads. If someone desperately needed to get to a hospital, and the only was over a private road, it would be immoral for the owner of the road to prevent the person in desperate need from using it.
1.1.2.1.1.1. Con: Immoral \(for someone\) but allowed \(for everyone\).
1.1.2.2. Con: This is not an issue of "breach of negative rights" \(i.e. "harm"\) as is implied by the original \(grandparent\) claim; this is an issue of omission, which at most is failure to meet positive rights.
This is made more clear by substituting words in the [If we simply...](https://www.kialo.com/argument/2214.2564) point:
"If we simply did nothing, \[homeless people\] would be able to voluntarily enter our \[homes\]. Preventing them from doing so requires actively using the threat of violence \[through law\] to stop them from accessing our \[homes\]."
1.1.2.3. Con: By that logic, if someone breaks into your house in the middle of the night you have no right to stop them because they might be fleeing abuse and you have no right to stop them from coming to a place of safety \(your house\). This is a clearly unreasonable conclusion, so the argument must not be sound.
1.1.2.3.1. Con: A difference in these examples is "might be fleeing abuse". Refugees are verified to be fleeing abuse, whereas with the house example the homeowner would not know.
1.1.2.3.2. Con: A more accurate example would be a large group knocking on a homeowners door and saying "please let me in, or we will suffer abuse". If the homeowner does not open the door, or lets in some but not all of the people outside, then the people outside may try to break into the house, or a neighbours house. In each case the homeowner has no legal duty to let the victim in, but it is fair to say there is a reasonable conclusion that they should help if they are able.
1.1.3. Con: This is not the case for all nations. If Italy bans refugees who arrive via the Mediterranean, this certainly causes harm. If Germany bans refugees who arrive via Austria, no direct harm is done as these refugees remain in a safe, high-income country.
1.1.4. Con: By this logic, refusing to accept a homeless person into your home when the weather is dangerous \(e.g. very cold\) would also be considered an active harm. This is unreasonable, as you have not contributed to the situation, do not seek to make it worse, there are many others in the same position to help, and you would have to take a huge risk by taking in a stranger.
1.1.4.1. Con: If there is a homeless person seeking shelter due to "dangerous weather", you are morally \(and probably legally\) obliged to help this person. You do not necessarily have to take them into your home \(e.g. there are organisations that can be contacted to help\), but you must not leave them outside to potentially die.
1.1.4.1.1. Con: There is no law forcing any household to take in any homeless person with exception of a few countries. For such persons, there are government-sponsored social institutions. Homeless people are a responsibility of society, not of an individual household.
1.1.4.2. Con: Refugees/Asylum seekers are not comparable to homeless people.
1.1.4.2.1. Pro: "A refugee, according to the [Convention](http://www.unhcr.org/3b66c2aa10), is someone who is unable or unwilling to return to their country of origin owing to a well-founded fear of being persecuted for reasons of race, religion,nationality, membership of a particular social group, or political opinion." If any person seeks refuge for other reasons, he loses that status and is not guaranteed access. High-income countries are economic, not safety havens.
1.1.4.2.2. Pro: A homeless person has no territory, nor land of origin \(in spacial terms\), so it is much harder to verify whether said person seeks safety in immediate proximity \(valid reason\) or in conjunction with other motives \(invalid reason\).
1.1.4.2.3. Pro: Refugees lose their right to ignore border enforcement once they reach safety, as their status is in regards to threat from harm from a country/religion/ideology/etc.
1.1.4.2.4. Pro: Homeless people retain their status regardless of weather conditions \(which are causal in the comparing claim's example\), as their vulnerability is due to their economic status, which cannot be escaped in a spacial sense.
1.1.4.3. Pro: On a similar basis to rights to property, a country can control who is eligible to enter its territory.
1.1.5. Con: By the same logic, every system of governance is committing acts of violence against its members as regulations and even taxation are ultimately enforced via the threat of violence in the case of non-compliance.
1.1.6. Pro: If somebody forcefully stops a starving person from reaching food, they have in effect killed that person. Similarly, if somebody stops a desperate refugee from reaching a safe place to live, they are morally responsible for whatever happens to that refugee.
1.1.6.1. Con: -> See 1.1.3.
1.1.6.2. Pro: If enabling a starving person to reach food does not significantly impact somebody's life, denying them is cruel. Denying refugees is not a prioritization of a state's primary responsibilities if it is a high-income country. It is just cruel.
1.1.6.3. Con: Such claim is conflating negative and positive harm/rights: not providing food may be immoral, but it is still an omission rather than positive/active harm. Similarly, it may be immoral/non-utilitarian to prevent refugees from entering a country, but it is not the right of those refugees to enter that country, just like it is not the right of homeless people to enter rich people's houses. Rich people are not morally responsible for what happens to homeless people.
1.1.6.3.1. Pro: One way to determine positive vs. negative harm is to ask the question: what if the rich person/country didn't exist? Would the homeless person/refugee truly be worse off if there were not somebody to build, maintain, and protect the house/country? If the answer is "no," then it is simply a case of moral omission—which should be condemned, but is principally different from active harm.
1.1.6.4. Con: This is not merely a question of stopping a starving person from reaching food. This situation is more of a starving person reaching 'your' food. Therefore, this statement assumes that a person has a responsibility of providing desperate people with 'their' things rather than ownerless items.
1.1.6.4.1. Con: It is by no means clear whether taking in and providing for refugees in a country has any tangible negative effect for the citizens of that country.
1.1.6.4.2. Pro: This presupposes that refugees have a moral claim to be able to access a country's resources and territory.
1.1.6.4.2.1. Pro: Restricting someone's freedom to go somewhere is not immoral when they have no right to go there in the first place. For example, there is nothing wrong with preventing trespassing.
1.1.6.4.2.1.1. Con: Preventing someone from trespassing is wrong if they are in desperate need and will die or suffer severe harm if they can't access your property.
1.1.6.4.2.1.1.1. Con: There are many intra-state laws that exist all over the world [against trespassing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trespass_in_English_law). States do not penalize a farmer for not letting a hungry person come in and eat his crops because the world operates on a system of every man having the right to the fruits of his labor.
1.1.6.4.2.1.1.2. Con: No one has a moral obligation to put the well-being of others before their own. It is therefore never wrong to prevent someone from trespassing if the occupant believes that allowing someone on their property might risk their personal safety, no matter how desperate the stranger may appear.
1.1.6.4.2.1.1.2.1. Con: It is unsure if refugees are a threat to the personal safety of citizens of countries housing them. Therefore it is morally unfair to let a person die just because that person might be a threat.
1.1.6.4.2.1.1.2.2. Con: It is false that we are never morally required to put the well-being of others before our own. We are not permitted to murder people, even if it would be advantageous to us to do so.
1.1.6.4.2.2. Pro: Borders are an inherent part of the world and of society. People do not have a default right to free movement everywhere.
1.1.6.4.2.2.1. Con: Borders as we know them originated in the 20th century, and free movement existed prior to that, though very few people made use of it due to the technological difficulties involved in travelling.
1.1.6.4.2.2.2. Pro: Many animals are [territorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territory_\(animal\)) - basically a primitive conception of borders.
1.1.6.4.2.2.2.1. Con: Basing human values on animal behavior is wrong since humans have an intellect and morality that animals lack.
1.1.6.4.2.2.2.1.1. Pro: Restricting the scope of moral consideration to members of one's own species is [morally acceptable](http://www.nyu.edu/classes/gmoran/WILLIAMS.pdf).
1.1.6.4.2.2.3. Con: Most political philosophy assumes that the default position is the "[state of nature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_nature)," which lacks borders.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4. Con: Borders are an instrumental part of society, set up because boundaries weren't respected. People can learn to respect boundaries and accept that we now exist in a more global and civil society.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.1. Pro: Several countries give people the right of [freedom to roam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_to_roam#Nordic_countries). The existence of this right, which gives a public right to freely access the wilderness, proves that society can function without borders.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.1.1. Pro: The fact that the right of freedom to roam works effectively, shows us that humans can be taught to respect property that they do not own, that borders aren't necessary for people to respect certain boundaries and that this is something that is desirable.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.2. Pro: Globalization has made the concept of nation-states into an obstruction rather than a benefit. Society would be more fair and better organized if this system was replaced by [civil society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_society).
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.2.1. Con: A civil society will not be implemented in the foreseeable future. Given that we are dealing with nation-states, we must consider what is of importance to nation-states, like the ability to enforce borders.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.2.1.1. Con: Many non-governmental organizations are already the biggest actors within many fields. The only obstacle for implementing civil society in the foreseeable future is nation-states.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.2.1.1.1. Pro: Global trade and economy is handled under the supervision of the [WTO](https://www.wto.org/) and the [IMF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund). The [UN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations) is the primary medium for diplomatic relations, maintains the international order and more than 4000 NGO's have some form of [consultative status](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_organizations_with_consultative_status_to_the_United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council) within the UN.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.2.1.1.2. Con: These NGOs only exist because they are created, supported, and funded by nation-states
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.2.1.1.2.1. Pro: NGOs rely on the existence of laws which protect them from theft, fraud, and so forth, and allow them to carry out their operations in a functioning economic system.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.2.2. Pro: Criticism of sovereignty and [nation-states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Westphalian_sovereignty#Modern_views_on_the_Westphalian_system) claims that it is obsolete and something that leads to rivalry and tension as opposed to community.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.3. Con: Borders are similarly not respected, even by developed countries. For example, in 2014 the Russian Federation made several military incursions into Ukrainian territory before finally [annexing Crimea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation), leading to an ongoing armed conflict between the two nations.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.3.1. Con: Despite condemnation from the West, the people of Crimea did [vote](http://time.com/26537/crimea-ukraine-russia-referendum-results/) overwhelmingly in favor of a referendum to secede from Ukraine and join Russia; and as such it can be argued that the annexation was lawful.
1.1.6.4.2.2.4.3.2. Con: This instance does not disprove that people and countries can learn to respect boundaries. It only proves that borders do not necessarily work as an effective tool of preventing entrance.
1.1.6.4.2.3. Con: The entire notion of ownership might be flawed. Simply because countries claim to own some resources does not mean that ownership is the only way of organizing society. In a society like a [marxist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism) one, it would be possible to have no ownership. Therefore states are acting immorally by unequally laying claim to resources that can be used to benefit desperate people.
1.1.6.4.2.3.1. Con: A marxist society simply is idealistic rather than realistic. Given that all people are self-interested, it is not practical/possible to "have no ownership," especially given problems such as tragedy of the commons and the necessity/threat of physical violence if someone lays claim to an unjust amount of resources \(e.g. taking others' food and hoarding it in a locked shed\).
In short, ownership is a necessary part of society, even if it has some flaws.
1.1.6.5. Con: Moral obligations and responsibilities between individuals differ from the moral obligations and responsibilities that exist between a state and various individuals.
1.1.6.5.1. Pro: It is morally right for a state to prioritize its own function and the well-being of its citizens above the well-being of refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.1. Pro: There are many people in high-income countries who are desperately in need of state assistance. It is morally acceptable to prioritise the welfare of these individuals over the welfare of refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.1.1. Pro: If the equal valuation of all human life would be a guide for our behavior, we would help not only refugees but many more people who suffer.
1.1.6.5.1.2. Con: Prioritizing the well being of own citizens over refugees is arbitrary, not inherent in the function of a state. If a dollar can save a refugee's life or improve a citizen's welfare, the first one ensures higher total value generated.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1. Con: A false analogy, since it ignores the massive amount of risks  that come with letting millions of refugees into the country. There are no risks at all with helping a fellow citizen who is already in the country.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1. Pro: Taking in refugees will increase criminality within host countries.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.1. Pro: A country taking in a large number of refugees is unable to provide decent living conditions and work opportunities. Because refugees end up living in very poor socioeconomic conditions, the risk that they will commit a crime is higher.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.1.1. Pro: A [study](http://www.government.se/articles/2017/02/facts-about-migration-and-crime-in-sweden/) by researchers at Stockholm University showed that the main difference in terms of criminal activity between immigrants and others in the population was due to differences in the socioeconomic conditions in which they grew up in Sweden.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.1.1.1. Con: While often used interchangeably, refugees, migrants, and asylum seekers are [not the same](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/aug/28/migrants-refugees-and-asylum-seekers-whats-the-difference). It is therefor questionable whether this study applies in this case.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.1.1.2. Con: Criminology studies on propensity to commit crime can't credibly control for culture factors, such as relative development, integration, isolationism \(e.g. ghetto formation\), etc. and are therefore one-sided.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.2. Pro: Refugees make up [about 1%](https://mediendienst-integration.de/migration/flucht-asyl/zahl-der-fluechtlinge.html) of the German population right now. In 2016, about 10% of the crimes relating to sexual self-determination were committed by refugees \([BMI, p. 75](https://www.bka.de/SharedDocs/Downloads/DE/Publikationen/PolizeilicheKriminalstatistik/2016/pks2016ImkBericht.pdf?__blob=publicationFile&v=5)\). Their share among these crimes is therefore vastly disproportionate and their link to crime potentially causal.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.3. Con: Out of the 208,344 [criminal offences](http://www.express.co.uk/news/world/644827/refugees-committed-crimes-Germany-migrant-crisis-last-year) committed by refugees in Germany 2015, over 165,000 were minor offences like taking public transportation without buying tickets.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.3.1. Con: This leaves over 40.000 non-minor offenses committed by refugees that would not have happened if they would not have been taken in.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.4. Con: In Germany between 2014 and 2015, a 440% increase in the number of refugees was accompanied by [only a 79%](http://www.express.co.uk/news/world/644827/refugees-committed-crimes-Germany-migrant-crisis-last-year) increase in crimes committed by immigrants.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.4.1. Con: Given the large numbers of existing immigrants, a 440% increase in refugees could have increased the number of immigrants by far less than 79%.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.4.2. Con: [Reports](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2017/04/12/why-some-migrants-are-more-likely-to-commit-crimes-than-others/?utm_term=.88805c535c80) suggest that asylum seekers who've been left in long-term limbo are increasingly likely to commit crimes. This implies that unless Germany becomes better at handling asylum-seekers, it is only a matter of time before crime rises exponentially.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.4.2.1. Con: This suggests that we should accept and integrate refugees as quickly as possible.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.5. Pro: Across Germany on [New Years’ Eve 2015](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2016/07/10/leaked-document-says-2000-men-allegedly-assaulted-1200-german-women-on-new-years-eve/?utm_term=.1ccf95d8888f),1,200 women were sexually assaulted, 24 were raped, and many others were physically restrained and robbed. The perpetrators were large groups of men gathered in crowds of up to 2,000. Of 120 identified suspects, more than half were new immigrants or asylum seekers.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.6. Pro: [2016 crime statistics](https://www.ft.com/content/b5a8867e-28ea-11e7-bc4b-5528796fe35c) for Germany showed that immigrants were responsible for 35% of pickpocketing cases, 11% of home break-ins, and nearly 15% of cases of grievous bodily harm. There were also 90% more immigrant suspects for violent crime cases than the year before.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.7. Pro: Refugees increase crime rates: in Germany, non-Germans commit [28% \(p. 8\)](https://www.bka.de/SharedDocs/Downloads/DE/Publikationen/JahresberichteUndLagebilder/KriminalitaetImKontextVonZuwanderung/KriminalitaetImKontextVonZuwanderung_2016.html;jsessionid=77EBA7AAAC877EE1EAC47F2DF0E25BD0.live2292?nn=62336) of alleged criminals but compose [13%](http://www.dw.com/en/more-foreigners-living-in-germany-than-ever-before/a-39495808) of the population.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.7.1. Con: [German criminologists](https://causa.tagesspiegel.de/gesellschaft/werden-migranten-haeufiger-straffaellig/passivitaet-foerdert-kriminalitaet.html) emphasize that migrants - and especially those who look "foreign" - are more likely to be accused of criminality that people who look like natives.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.7.2. Pro: The quantity of violent crime has been stable or declining in Germany for decades. As a result of the recent influx of refugees, it is once again rising. Without the crimes committed by recent migrants, this [would not be the case](http://www.zeit.de/2017/17/kriminalitaet-fluechtlinge-zunahme-gewalttaten-statistik).
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.7.3. Con: According to the Federal Criminal Police, migrants from Iraq, Afghanistan and Syria - were most of the recent arrivals come from - commit a disproportionally low number of crimes. Disproportionally high numbers are comitted by people from the Balkans, the Maghreb and North Africa \([BKA, p. 5f.](https://www.bka.de/SharedDocs/Downloads/DE/Publikationen/JahresberichteUndLagebilder/KriminalitaetImKontextVonZuwanderung/kernaussagenZuKriminalitaetImKontextVonZuwanderungI-IIQuartal2017.html;jsessionid=77EBA7AAAC877EE1EAC47F2DF0E25BD0.live2292?nn=62336)\).
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.7.4. Pro: The vast majority of crimes are committed by men between the ages of 14 and 30. Since refugees disproportionately come from this demographic, they are [disproportionately likely to commit crimes](http://www.dw.com/en/are-refugees-more-criminal-than-the-average-german-citizen/a-38371284).
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.7.5. Con: These crime rates are not necessarily the result of refugees being intrinsically more likely to commit crimes, but also of the circumstances in which they live: without work, without much expendable income, without much to do. Crime rates might be lower if refugees were helped to establish daily routines and a self-sufficient lifestyle.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.7.5.1. Pro: The situation of many refugees in Germany is [marked by](http://www.spiegel.de/international/germany/asylum-shelters-in-germany-struggle-with-refugee-violence-a-1056393.html) "day after day of monotony and emptiness with nothing meaningful to do"; as a result, [many go](https://www.thelocal.de/20160220/refugees-in-germany-stewing-in-boredom-as-they-await-integration) "crazy with boredom".
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.8. Pro: Refugees committed more than [200,000](https://www.express.co.uk/news/world/644827/refugees-committed-crimes-Germany-migrant-crisis-last-year) crimes 2015 in Germany.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.9. Con: Since refugees typically end up living in concentrated neighbourhoods with other refugees, we might expect that the victims of crimes committed by refugees are other refugees. The host country is not harmed, and the refugees who are victims of crimes are still left better off than having not been accepted.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.9.1. Pro: In 2/3 of the [240](http://www.express.co.uk/news/world/644827/refugees-committed-crimes-Germany-migrant-crisis-last-year) attempted murders by immigrants in Germany 2015, the victims were of the same nationality as the assailant. In only one of these cases was a German killed.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.10. Con: According to the interior minister of Germany, the vast majority of immigrants are law-abiding. Recent [figures](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2017/04/25/migrant-crime-germany-rises-50-per-cent-new-figures-show/) from the interior ministry shows that just 1% of migrants account for 40% of the crimes committed by migrants.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.10.1. Con: The distribution of crimes does not matter; the point is still that allowing in refugees leads to an increase in crime rates.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.10.1.1. Con: The distribution of crimes does matter.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.10.1.1.1. Pro: If people see that the crime rate within the refugee population is high, they may believe that refugees are more likely to be criminals. This is inaccurate and misleading if only a small percentage of the refugees account for most of the crimes.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.10.1.1.2. Pro: The criminality is much more easily managed and dealt with if the crime is concentrated to a small portion of all refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.10.1.1.2.1. Pro: A wide distribution of crime would suggest that the root of the problem of criminality among refugees is due to the circumstances of the refugees' situation, something that is difficult to fix effectively.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.10.1.1.3. Pro: The only asylum seekers that are disproportionately likely to commit crimes are those who know they are unlikely to be accepted \(eg refugees from the Balkans\). Therefore, having open acceptance policies could make refugees less likely to commit crimes.
1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.10.1.1.4. Pro: If people believe that refugees are more likely to be criminal when they see statistics of the crime rate, they will advocate for a solution that deals with the refugees as a whole. This would be an ineffective solution when the crime is concentrated to small group within the refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.2.2. Con: Democracies usually indicate or imply that their efforts are to serve, first and foremost, the citizens of the respective democracy.
1.1.6.5.1.2.2.1. Pro: The [Preamble](https://constitutioncenter.org/interactive-constitution/preamble) of the American Constitution states that the document and its purposes are dedicated "to ourselves and our Posterity", not the citizens of any other nation.
1.1.6.5.1.2.2.2. Pro: The text over the entrance of the [German parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichstag_building) reads "Dem Deutschen Volke" \("To the German People"\), implying that the building and the political body it houses are meant to serve the German people, not those of any other nation.
1.1.6.5.1.2.2.3. Pro: The second article of the [French Constitution](http://www.conseil-constitutionnel.fr/conseil-constitutionnel/english/constitution/constitution-of-4-october-1958.25742.html) states that the principle of government shall be "of the people, by the people and for the people", which supposedly refers to the French people and not those of other nations.
1.1.6.5.1.2.3. Pro: Most states have committed themselves to human rights in general, not those of their citizens exclusively. This implies that they value  individuals equally, regardless of nationality.
1.1.6.5.1.2.3.1. Pro: The [German constitution](https://www.gesetze-im-internet.de/englisch_gg/englisch_gg.html#p0021) refers in its first three articles to "human dignity", "peace and of justice in the world" and "every person", and states that no one shall we disfavoured because of "homeland and origin".
1.1.6.5.1.2.3.2. Pro: All countries have signed the Universal Declaration of Human Rights which [refers to](http://www.un.org/en/universal-declaration-human-rights/) the "inherent dignity and of the equal and inalienable rights of all members of the human family".
1.1.6.5.1.3. Pro: Sovereign states, in the way we understand them today, exist to protect the interests and freedoms of the people within them. If taking in refugees is likely to be harmful to a population, it cannot be considered immoral for a country to take an action that prioritizes the people it exists to protect over those of other countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4. Pro: Taking in refugees has negative consequences for high-income countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1. Pro: Refugees threaten the national identity of countries that host them.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1. Pro: Countries should focus on accepting people with whom they share cultural values and traditions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.1. Con: Following this logic, of the world's high-income countries organized in the OECD, only Turkey should take in refugees as most of today's refugees have a Muslim and Arab background. This would absolve the first world from any obligations.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.2. Con: It is not clear where to draw the line between similar values and traditions and different values and traditions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.2.1. Pro: According to the German government, Islam "[belongs to Germany](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-germany-islam-merkel/merkel-says-islam-belongs-to-germany-ahead-of-dresden-rally-idUSKBN0KL1S020150112)". The country hosts [about 4.5 million](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Germany) Muslims. It is not clear whether the Muslim background of many refugees, nevertheless, is too different from Germany's culture.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.2.1.1. Pro: German culture is diverse and has always been diverse due to the history of the country. Muslims are, just like all adherents to large major religions very diverse.To say muslims are to different than germans is to generalise all muslims and all germans.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.2.2. Pro: Turkey is an [overwhelmingly Sunni Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_Turkey) country. It is not clear whether this means that refugees from Shia countries should be rejected, for example from Iraq. Both have Muslim backgrounds - yet these branches of Islam often clash.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.3. Pro: To some extent it is important that people have commonalities, for society to work.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.4. Con: While cultural identity is important and should be preserved, one ought not to strap oneself to a present view of culture. Most cultures, as individual and specific as they may be, are an eclectic mix and match of previous cultural and ethnic groups that inhabited/traded/passed through etc. a region. Therefore, allowing people with different cultural values into a country only furthers the development of a culture.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.5. Con: Europe's refugee crisis is not obviously an example of cultural incompatibility at work. [Success stories](http://m.spiegel.de/international/germany/a-1160939.html) are commonplace.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.6. Con: Cultural incompatibility is temporary, as cultures and cultural expressions change over time. This adaptation toward compatibility is accelerated by cultural exchange.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.6.1. Pro: Syria is often used as an example of a culture incompatible with Western values, but "immigrants from Syria who live in the United States are in fact [doing very well](https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/immigration/reports/2016/12/13/294851/syrian-immigrants-in-the-united-states-a-receiving-community-for-todays-refugees/). They are learning English, getting good jobs, owning homes, and starting businesses at impressive rates."
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.6.1.1. Con: US immigration programs are fairly selective, so the Syrian immigrants living in the US are unlikely to be representative of the population of Syrian refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.6.2. Pro: [This report](http://www.migrationpolicy.org/research/immigrants-united-states-how-well-are-they-integrating-society) documents how "just as previous waves of immigrants eventually found their way into the mainstream of American life \(even those who were initially considered 'unassimilable'\), the recent inflow of immigrants is integrating reasonably well."
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7. Pro: Immigrants that do not share cultural values and traditions with their host country are more likely to struggle with integration.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7.1. Pro: This can, from a long-term perspective, entrench the segregation of ethnic groups through a socioeconomic gap, where the ethnic minorities are the group with the lowest socioeconomic status.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7.2. Pro: Immigrants who aren't familiar with the culture and values of the host country is likely to have a harder time getting a job.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7.2.1. Pro: [Social networks](https://www.forbes.com/sites/adigaskell/2017/09/11/using-social-networks-to-advance-your-career/#773e5dc50a66) are incredibly important for job opportunities. Immigrants that aren't familiar with culture and values of the host country may struggle to establish proper social networks that can lead to job opportunities.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7.3. Pro: It is likely that many of the citizens in the host country will have biases against immigrants due to fear as their culture and values are unfamiliar.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7.3.1. Pro: This means that it is more likely that immigrants are socially excluded by the majority.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7.4. Con: The population of countries are already getting more diverse due to globalization. As multicultural societies become more established, the issues casued due to cultural differences will decrease.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7.4.1. Pro: Cultural diversity [can](https://www.kaplanuniversity.edu/news-resources/what-is-cultural-diversity/) lead to gradual acceptance over time. Immediate bad reaction to diversity only brings to the forefront bigotry that already exists. Diversity can eventually lead to overcoming the bigotry and developing tolerance.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7.5. Con: Issues of integration should be considered a secondary issue to the importance of helping those that needs the most help. Countries should prioritize helping those that needs help the most even if it means accepting refugees that will have a harder time integrating.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.8. Pro: Many high-income countries, like [Japan](https://berkleycenter.georgetown.edu/posts/ethnicity-in-japan) and [Denmark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographics_of_Denmark#Ethnic_groups), are highly ethnically and culturally homogeneous. Accepting Muslim refugees threatens the national identities of these countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.9. Pro: China is [not accepting](http://foreignpolicy.com/2016/02/26/china-host-syrian-islam-refugee-crisis-migrant/) any Syrian refugees as it sees that as interference with other countries' domestic affairs. China generally focuses its efforts on groups close to them.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.9.1. Con: China - an authoritarian regime ruled by a single party and with [severe human rights abuses](https://www.hrw.org/world-report/2018/country-chapters/china-and-tibet) - is hardly a country that should be taken as an example for morally correct behavior.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.2. Con: Almost all European countries have Muslim populations that make up [under 10%](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/07/19/5-facts-about-the-muslim-population-in-europe/) of the total population. Considering about 511 million people live in the EU alone, even accepting all Syrian refugees would not make a huge impact.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.2.1. Con: Muslims in the [UK](https://www.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/571996/annual-report.pdf) commit a vastly disproportionate number of [crimes](http://researchbriefings.files.parliament.uk/documents/SN04334/SN04334.pdf) which tends to undermine their reputation as a community and highlights that although their population may be relatively small their negative impact is much higher.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.2.1.1. Con: Anti-Muslim racism is on the [rise](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/home-news/british-muslims-face-worst-job-discrimination-of-any-minority-group-9893211.html) in the UK, and Muslims have reported increased [discrimination](http://www.fairuk.org/docs/OSI2004%209_Justice1.pdf) by the justice system \(p. 257\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.2.2. Con: Most refugees want to live in [northern countries](https://theconversation.com/why-dont-refugees-just-stay-in-turkey-or-greece-we-asked-them-70257) and form communities in the cities. Allowing them all to come will cause problems.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.2.2.1. Pro: The Brussels neighborhood of [Molenbeek](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/04/12/opinion/the-islamic-state-of-molenbeek.html) has become infamous because Islamic terrorists lived and planned their attacks there.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.2.2.2. Con: These problems could be alleviated if said northern countries improved their immigrant integration policies, as this would help prevent the feelings of cultural isolation that have led to increased radicalization levels in places like Molenbeek.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.2.2.3. Pro: The majority of refugees doesn't want to stay in Turkey or Greece, but states that their ideal destination countries are Germany, Sweden, and the UK.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.2.2.4. Pro: [Mannheim](https://www.theguardian.com/cities/2016/apr/11/refuge-cities-mannheim-germany-refugee-crisis-sanctuary-or-ghetto), Germany, has created a "city within the city" for refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.3. Con: Europe is becoming [more](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/phil-zuckerman/religion-declining-secula_b_9889398.html) [secular](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2015/06/22/what-is-each-countrys-second-largest-religious-group/). It is unlikely that Islam will substantially affect public life.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.3.1. Con: The share of the EU's population who are Muslim is [growing steadily](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/07/19/5-facts-about-the-muslim-population-in-europe/). Even if the EU as a whole is secularising, the influence of Islam specifically is still increasing.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.3.1.1. Con: There is nothing to suggest that secularisation does not happen to muslims. Secularisation happens in all religions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.3.2. Con: 28% of Muslims polled for a French [study](https://www.gatestoneinstitute.org/9058/france-islamization) say that Islamic law \(sharia\) is more important to them than the common law of the French republic.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.3.2.1. Con: That 72% of people who identify as Muslims think otherwise, suggests that most still prefer France to be a secular society.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.4. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.6.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.5. Con: While refugees and migrants can influence a country's demographic, to say that they threaten its national identity in a significant way seems unlikely.  In fact, social interests of corporations \(i.e. the social influence of facebook, snapchat, instagram, linkedin, and other social media platforms\) influence the national identity of our culture in a much more significant manner.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.6. Con: All national identities are a result of integration, not homogeneity.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.7. Con: A person themself can threaten the national identity of a company as they are possibly not interested in promoting it, but criticise and talk badly about it. But they are not a refugee. We can't state every refugee threatens the national identity. Some of them will, others won't, just like the native population.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.8. Con: The share of migrants is  lower then 15% of the population in both the [US](https://www.census.gov/newsroom/pdf/cspan_fb_slides.pdf) and [most EU countries](http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/index.php/File:Foreign-born_population_by_country_of_birth,_1_January_2016_\(%C2%B9\).png). In addition, migrants are split into many different groups. Therefore, democracy can hardly be heavily affected.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.9. Pro: High income countries are mostly democracies, and accepting immigrants that have very different values \(for example believe countries should be governed by the Sharia\) can change the nature of society once those people \(and their children\) vote.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10. Pro: The influx of refugees from foreign regions inevitably means that the culture of high-income countries will change over time.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.1. Con: There is no such thing as a unique and stable culture in the West.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.1.1. Pro: Europe as we know it and its culture were in part shaped by influences from abroad, for example through invasions by [Mongols](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe) as well as [Persians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Persian_invasion_of_Greece).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.2. Con: Western culture has been the foundation for crusades, colonialism and World Wars. It would be a positive development for this culture to change through outside influences.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3. Pro: Most of the refugees in recent years have been fleeing from [Muslim-majority countries](https://www.worldvision.org/refugees-news-stories/forced-flee-top-5-countries-refugees) in the Middle East and North Africa, thus high-income countries that have accepted refugees are seeing a marked increase in their Muslim populations. This means that said countries will likely experience an upsurge in Islamic influence.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1. Pro: As refugees are predominantly Muslim they - along with existing Muslim populations - threaten the national identities of Western countries by remaining a separate, easily identifiable group that tries to carve out public space for itself and exert political power.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.1. Pro: Muslim populations in Western countries are not evenly distributed, but are highly concentrated in certain parts of large cities, where they visibly dominate the public sphere. In some cases, these areas have become "[sensitive areas](https://www.algemeiner.com/2015/12/07/the-truth-about-muslim-no-go-zones-in-europe/)" \(also referred to as ["no-go zones"](https://www.gatestoneinstitute.org/2367/european-muslim-no-go-zones)\) where government representatives like [firefighters](http://www.breitbart.com/london/2017/09/09/swedish-firemen-let-building-burn-attacked-no-go-zone/) \(see [police press release](https://web.archive.org/web/20170912073824/https://polisen.se/Skane/Aktuellt/Handelser/Skane/2017-09-07-2051-Brand-Malmo/)\), [ambulance workers](http://www.dagensmedicin.se/artiklar/2014/11/11/ambulansfack-vill-ha-militarutrustning/) and [police](https://www.jihadwatch.org/2016/10/france-police-need-extra-protection-when-entering-muslim-no-go-zones) are often attacked.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.1.1. Con: The claims about the supposed 'no-go zones' have been publicly debunked as inaccurate reporting and the source, Gatestone Institute has been criticized for alleged [anti-Muslim bias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gatestone_Institute#Allegations_of_anti-Muslim_bias).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.1.2. Con: None of the sources above support the statement that there is a connection between Muslims and the attacks on public servants.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2. Pro: Muslim populations in Western countries largely vote left: [93% in France for Hollande 2012 \(p. 9\)](http://opinionlab.opinion-way.com/dokumenty/Sondage_jour_de_vote_T2_SOCIOLOGIE_DU_VOTE_2_1.pdf), [89% in Denmark 2011](http://www.dr.dk/Nyheder/Indland/2009/04/23/161207.htm), [80% in Germany 2012](https://liebbu.files.wordpress.com/2012/08/wertewelten-2012-pressemitteilung.pdf), [74% in the US for Kerry 2004 \(p.41\)](http://pewresearch.org/files/old-assets/pdf/muslim-americans.pdf), [66% lean Democrat 2017](http://www.pewforum.org/2017/07/26/findings-from-pew-research-centers-2017-survey-of-us-muslims/pf_2017-06-26_muslimamericans-00-01/) - this disturbs the balance of power in those countries. Since the Muslim voting demographic is growing, they will become increasingly more influential in the future.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1. Pro: Muslim voters tend to vote for parties that advocate open borders for refugees, which effectively enables an influx of more Muslims into high-income countries. This is in opposition to the majority of the general populace, who in most high-income countries favors a [stop of Muslim immigration](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/most-europeans-want-muslim-ban-immigration-control-middle-east-countries-syria-iran-iraq-poll-a7567301.html).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.1. Pro: As of 2016, more than 90% of people with Turkish roots in Germany - who make up [two thirds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Germany#Demographics) of the country's Muslims - declared a political preference for one of the three left-wing parties in Germany \([BAMF, p. 14](https://www.svr-migration.de/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/SVR_FB_Parteipraeferenz.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.1.1. Pro: Of all major German parties, the three left-wing parties had the [most welcoming stance](http://www.dw.com/en/afd-cdu-spd-where-do-german-parties-stand-on-refugees-asylum-and-immigration/a-40610988) towards refugees in the country's 2017 general election.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.1.2. Con: It is questionable how significant this party preference is in the context of Germany's refugee policies. No major party calls for a stop of taking in refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.1.2.1. Con: Yet the left-wing and right-wing parties disagree on details: the conservative parties [agreed to implement](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/10/09/world/europe/germany-merkel-refugees.html) a cap on total number of refugees and [wants to restrict](http://www.dw.com/en/afd-cdu-spd-where-do-german-parties-stand-on-refugees-asylum-and-immigration/a-40610988) family reunions of refugees on Germany.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2. Con: If the majority of citizens in a country oppose open borders for refugees, the preferences of Muslims in this area won't be implemented due to their small electoral weight. This is therefore a non-issue.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2.1. Pro: Muslims are hardly a significant political force in high-income countries, even under the assumption that all of them are able to vote, turn out to vote and cast the same vote.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2.1.1. Pro: The share of Muslims among the population in major European countries is relatively low: [7.5%](http://The share of Muslims among the population in major European countries is relatively low: 7.5% in France) in France, around [5.5%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Germany) in Germany, [5%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_England) in England and [2.3%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Italy#Present_day) in Italy. In the US, their share stands at [1%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_the_United_States).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2.1.2. Con: The Muslim populations in high income-countries is forecast to grow significantly. In Europe, it will [almost double](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/apr/02/muslim-population-growth-christians-religion-pew) by 2050 from 6% to around 10%.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2.1.2.1. Con: Regardless of the growth elsewhere, even in 2050 Muslims will make up [merely 2.1%](http://www.pewforum.org/2015/04/02/religious-projections-2010-2050/) of the American population.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2.1.2.2. Con: These numbers hardly tell the whole story. Assuming people's behavior is shaped by their religious affiliation, Christians will still dominate as a majority in the US, Germany, Italy, Poland and Belgium or make up over 40% of the population in the UK and France in 2050 \([PEW, p. 234f.](http://www.pewforum.org/files/2015/03/PF_15.04.02_ProjectionsFullReport.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2.1.3. Pro: Many of the arguments about Muslims' political influence are the outcome of [misconceptions](https://www.theguardian.com/society/datablog/2016/dec/13/europeans-massively-overestimate-muslim-population-poll-shows) of Muslim's role in high-income countries. People in the US tend to grossly overestimate the Muslim share of their country's population by a factor of 17, people in Italy by a factor of 5, people in Germany, the UK and France by a factor of 4.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2.1.4. Pro: Once the age structure of Muslims in Europe is taken into account, their political weight shrinks further. In England, for example a third of Muslims is under 15 years old and unable to vote in the first place \([MCB, p. 16](https://www.mcb.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/MCBCensusReport_2015.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2.1.5. Pro: Once the nationality of these Muslims is taken into account, their political weight shrinks further. Only about half the Muslims in Germany - [2.5%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Germany) of the whole population - have German nationality and can vote.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.2. Pro: Muslims largely vote for parties that promote generous welfare programs, which disproportionately benefit Muslim communities.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.2.1. Con: Each and every citizen in a democracy is assumed and has the right to vote for political parties that provide them with benefits of some kind. The decision of Muslims to do so should not be singled out.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.2.2. Pro: Muslim populations in high-income countries tend to be in positions where they profit more than other groups from generous welfare.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.2.2.1. Pro: In the UK, almost half the Muslim population lives in poverty, which is twice the share of members of other religious affiliations. The unemployment rate for Muslims at 7.2% was almost twice that of the general population in 2011 \([JRF, p. 34](https://www.jrf.org.uk/sites/default/files/jrf/migrated/files/Reducing-poverty-reviews-FULL_0.pdf); [MCB, p. 58](https://www.mcb.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/MCBCensusReport_2015.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.3. Con: Other groups, too, do this and strive to promote their own legitimate interests. Muslims should not be singled out in this context.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.3.1. Pro: In the United States, the same argument could be made about the tendencies of Jews and Mormons to [vote "as a block"](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/02/23/u-s-religious-groups-and-their-political-leanings/ft_16-02-22_religionpoliticalaffiliation_640px-2/) - and especially so as both religions have [more followers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_the_United_States#Statistics) in the US than Islam. Yet these voting tendencies are not perceived as a problem in those cases.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.3.1.1. Pro: American Hindus and Buddhists vote as a block to a [even higher degree](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/02/23/u-s-religious-groups-and-their-political-leanings/ft_16-02-22_religionpoliticalaffiliation_640px-2/) than Muslims and represent a [similar share](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_the_United_States#Statistics) of the population as Muslims. Yet this is usually not perceived as problematic.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.3.2. Con: Muslims are a growing foreign element in the West that will permanently change the balance of power within Western societies. While there may be other groups that also vote as a block, these are either not growing significantly, or are also regarded as a threat to national identity, e.g. Hispanic immigrants in the U.S.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.4. Con: Even if Muslim politicians come into positions of power this can hardly be assumed to predetermine their political decisions, for example based on the general preferences of Muslim voters.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.4.1. Pro: According to surveys, half of all Muslims in Britain think that homosexuality [should be illegal](https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2016/apr/11/british-muslims-strong-sense-of-belonging-poll-homosexuality-sharia-law). Yet the country's most prominent Muslim politician - Sadiq Khan, mayor of London - repeatedly [voted in favor](https://www.theyworkforyou.com/mp/11878/sadiq_khan/tooting/divisions?policy=826) of gay marriage and gay rights.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.4.2. Pro: As of 2012, half of Germany's population with a Turkish background stated in a survey that homosexuality is a disease \([INFO, p. 73](https://web.archive.org/web/20121011112234/https://d171.keyingress.de/multimedia/document/228.pdf)\). Nevertheless, [all six Muslim members](https://www.haaretz.com/world-news/europe/1.798712) of the German parliament \(five of them with Turkish roots\) voted in favor of legalizing gay marriage in 2016.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.5. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.1.2.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6. Pro: Admitting new voting demographics to a country that reliably vote a certain way is a threat to national identity.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.1. Pro: Through mass immigration, the vote can be changed much faster than through argument or disparate fertility of voting populations.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.1.1. Con: In the context of the recent influx of refugees to high-income countries, the number of naturalization is very limited.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.1.1.1. Pro: In Germany, only [about 8.000 people](https://www.destatis.de/DE/PresseService/Presse/Pressemitteilungen/2017/06/PD17_195_12511.html) from countries where refugees commonly originate from \(Syria, Iraq, Afghanistan\) were naturalized in 2016. This is a mere 7% of that year's naturalizations and makes up 0.1 of the [German electorate](https://www.bundeswahlleiter.de/info/presse/mitteilungen/bundestagswahl-2017/01_17_wahlberechtigte.html).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.1.1.2. Pro: In the United States, only [about 24.000 people](https://www.dhs.gov/immigration-statistics/yearbook/2015) from countries where refugees commonly originate from \(Syria, Iraq, Afghanistan, Somalia, Sudan\) were naturalized in 2015. This is a mere 3% of that year's naturalizations and makes up 0.1 of the [American electorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voter_turnout_in_the_United_States_presidential_elections#Turnout_statistics).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.1.1.3. Pro: In the UK, only [about 7.000 people](https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/immigration-statistics-october-to-december-2016/citizenship) from countries where refugees commonly originate from \(Syria, Iraq, Afghanistan, Somalia, Sudan\) were naturalized in 2016. This is a mere 5% of that year's naturalizations and makes up 0.2 of the [British electorate](https://www.ons.gov.uk/peoplepopulationandcommunity/elections/electoralregistration/bulletins/electoralstatisticsforuk/2015).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.1.1.4. Con: These numbers are likely to increase as refugees spend more time in their new countries of residence.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.1.1.4.1. Pro: In the case of Germany, and during 2016, [more than 10%](https://www.destatis.de/DE/PresseService/Presse/Pressemitteilungen/2017/06/PD17_195_12511.html) of the citizens of countries where refugees commonly originate from \(Syria, Iraq, Afghanistan\) and who had stayed in Germany for more than ten years, naturalized.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.2. Pro: There are many more people in the world who would be willing to immigrate to high-income countries, and who would vote predictably for left-wing parties, than there are currently citizens of these countries. Immigration policies can therefore be used to import left-wing voters. Doing so would then change the focus of those parties to the new voting populations, changing their policies to suit the new arrivals.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3. Con: Refugees usually cannot vote unless they become citizens. the immediate political influence of refugees, even if they are Muslims, is therefore limited.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.1. Con: A significant share of refugees will stay and eventually become citizens who are able to vote.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.1.1. Pro: Mainstream discussion revolves around what can be done to better integrate them into society, and how they should be able to bring their families to their host countries. Since left-wing parties stand to gain vote shares by that process, they have a vested interest to pursue this course.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.1.2. Con: The reason why talk about sending refugees back to their home countries once they become safe hardly features in the political discourse is because it is irrelevant. Neither of the major countries of origin of today's refugees is expected to become safe for return in the near future.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.1.2.1. Pro: Where feasible, talk about sending rejected refugees back does actually feature in the political discourse. Parts of Germany's governing CSU/CDU party consider regions of Afghanistan [safe enough for return](http://www.dw.com/en/germanys-cdu-party-members-laud-return-of-rejected-asylum-seekers-to-afghanistan/a-40030757).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.1.3. Pro: While Angela Merkel once said that [refugees must return home](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-europe-migrants-germany-refugees/germanys-merkel-says-refugees-must-return-home-once-war-is-over-idUSKCN0V80IH), she also said that 70% of ex-Yugoslavian refugees returned home, implying that 30% stayed and were not forced to leave.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.1.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.1.1.4.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.1.5. Pro: Current deportation practices in Western countries are such that even rejected asylum applicants and illegal migrants are not rigorously deported.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.1.5.1. Pro: Germany has given asylum to a quarter million Afghans; 10,000 have been ordered to leave, but only [261](http://www.dw.com/en/germanys-cdu-party-members-laud-return-of-rejected-asylum-seekers-to-afghanistan/a-40030757) have been deported in the first half of 2017.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.1.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.7. Con: It is not clear how a political preference for established left-wing parties represents a threat to the national identity of high-income countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.7.1. Pro: The parties favored by Muslims in high-income countries have decade-long histories and were part of numerous governments \(e.g. the SPD in Germany and Labour in the UK\). They can hardly be considered as undermining a country's identity.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.8. Con: The idea of an electoral balance between conservative and liberal forces in high-income countries that could be swayed more than usual by Muslim influences is unrealistic. Larger shifts in the balance already occur naturally.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.8.1. Pro: In the United States, the share of the popular vote won by Republicans in the House of Representatives has varied during the past decade between [43%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_2008) and [52%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_2010), and in the Senate between [42%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate_elections,_2016) and [54%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate_elections,_2012). Even when Muslims make up [2%](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/01/06/a-new-estimate-of-the-u-s-muslim-population/) of the US population in 2050, their influence will be negligible compared to these already occurring shifts.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.8.2. Pro: In Germany, the share of the vote won by left-wing parties \(SPD, The Left, Green Party\) varied between [52%](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bundestagswahl_1998) in 1998 and [39%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_federal_election,_2017) in 2017. Even if a growing Muslim population produces electoral shifts, these are not unprecedented.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.8.3. Pro: In the UK, share of the popular vote won by the Labour Party during the last decade has varied between [29%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010) in 2010 and [40%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017) in 2017. Even a growing share of Muslims in the UK is not capable of effecting political shifts disproportionate to this.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.9. Con: Even if this were true, this move of the electoral balance to the left would be more than counter-acted by the aging population of high-income countries and the tendency of older people to vote for conservative parties.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.9.1. Pro: In the recent elections in countries like [Germany](https://wahl.tagesschau.de/wahlen/2017-09-24-BT-DE/umfrage-alter.shtml), [the United States](https://ropercenter.cornell.edu/polls/us-elections/how-groups-voted/groups-voted-2016/) and [the UK](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/datablog/ng-interactive/2017/jun/20/young-voters-class-and-turnout-how-britain-voted-in-2017), age and a tendency to vote for conservative parties and candidates have correlated reliably.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.9.2. Pro: The Muslim population of Europe will increase [by 4%](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/apr/02/muslim-population-growth-christians-religion-pew) and that of the US [by 1%](http://www.pewforum.org/2015/04/02/religious-projections-2010-2050/) until 2050. At the same time, the share of the population aged over 65 will [increase by](http://www.pewglobal.org/2014/01/30/chapter-2-aging-in-the-u-s-and-other-countries-2010-to-2050/) 12% in Germany, 9% in France, and 8% in Britain and the US.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.10. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.6.3.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.11. Con: Muslims vote as individuals. They do not vote as a block to any higher degree than other individuals whose voting preference tends to correlate with certain socio-demographic features.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.11.1. Pro: As has been emphasized for the recent elections in [France](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/order-from-chaos/2017/04/27/is-there-a-muslim-vote-in-france/), [the UK](http://www.politics.co.uk/comment-analysis/2017/05/04/searching-for-the-muslim-vote) and [Germany](https://www.welt.de/politik/deutschland/article168718779/Wen-waehlen-Muslime-bei-der-Bundestagswahl.html), there is no thing such as a "Muslim vote". Muslim individuals vote based on political, social and economic preferences, not based on their religious affiliation.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.11.2. Con: Religions and their world views influence political behavior in significant ways, for example by providing guidance on questions of values, morals and legitimacy \([Fox, p. 56ff.](https://books.google.co.kr/books/about/An_Introduction_to_Religion_and_Politics.html?id=Q3Y2fE6Ptq8C&redir_esc=y)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.11.2.1. Con: Other voices [oppose](https://bostonreview.net/politics/elizabeth-shakman-hurd-myth-muslim-country) the idea that a religious affiliation with Islam predetermines political behavior in a predetermined fashion and, in particular, in regards to violence.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.11.3. Con: Muslims in the USA lean heavily to the Democrat and big government side \([Dems vs. GOP 67% vs. 6% in 2016](https://www.voanews.com/a/american-muslim-voters-presidential-election/3549727.html), [big vs. small gov 70% vs. 21%, see page 41](http://pewresearch.org/files/old-assets/pdf/muslim-americans.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3. Con: Muslims are not one group but as diverse as other major religions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.1. Con: Muslims, in general, value their religion greatly.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.1.1. Pro: [Two thirds](http://www.pewforum.org/2015/11/03/chapter-1-importance-of-religion-and-religious-beliefs/) of American Muslims say that Islam is very important to them, another 24% that it is somewhat important.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.1.1.1. Con: American Muslims are not unique in this regard or should be singled out for it. The corresponding numbers for American Christians [are even higher](http://www.pewforum.org/2015/11/03/chapter-1-importance-of-religion-and-religious-beliefs/) at 68% and 25%.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.2. Pro: Muslims in high-income countries are a socio-economically diverse group. These factors shape their lives just as religion does.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.2.1. Pro: Among American Muslims, the share of those with an annual income of less than $30.000 as well as of those earning more than $150.000 are [both larger](http://www.pewforum.org/2017/07/26/demographic-portrait-of-muslim-americans/) than among the population as a whole.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.2.2. Con: Especially in Europe, the Muslim population tends to be at the lower end of the economic ladder.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.2.2.1. Pro: In Britain, Muslims have twice the national rate of unemployment and almost half of Muslims live in the 10% most deprived \([MCB, p. 46, 58](https://www.mcb.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/MCBCensusReport_2015.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.3. Pro: How Muslims in high-income countries see and live their religion varies.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.3.1. Pro: As of 2006, [only a quarter](http://www.pewglobal.org/2006/06/22/the-great-divide-how-westerners-and-muslims-view-each-other/) of Muslims in Spain stated in a survey that there is an inherent conflict between being a devout Muslim and living in a modern society, whereas almost half of Muslims in Britain did.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.3.2. Pro: [Two thirds](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2017/08/28/u-s-muslims-are-religiously-observant-but-open-to-multiple-interpretations-of-islam/) of American Muslims believe that there are multiple true interpretations of Islam.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.4. Con: Most refugees who are Muslims come from countries where a particular and strict attitude towards Islam is prevalent.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.4.1. Pro: Among the Muslims in Afghanistan and Iraq, [99% and - respectively - 91%](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2017/08/09/muslims-and-islam-key-findings-in-the-u-s-and-around-the-world/) believe that sharia should be the official law of their country.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.4.1.1. Con: At the same time: where Islam is not the majority religion, a [far smaller share](http://www.pewforum.org/2013/04/30/the-worlds-muslims-religion-politics-society-overview/) of Muslims hold this opinion. Support for the implementation of sharia law might thus shrink as Muslim refugees arrive in high-income countries with a Muslim majority.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.5. Pro: Depending on where Muslim refugees come from, they are likely to hold very different opinions on various issues.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.5.1. Pro: On issues like whether sharia should be the law of the land, whether women have to wear a veil and whether there should be restrictions on women and men in the same workplaces, attitudes among Muslims [vary](http://www.pewglobal.org/2008/09/17/chapter-5-muslim-views-on-gender-issues/) [widely](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2017/08/09/muslims-and-islam-key-findings-in-the-u-s-and-around-the-world/) across countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4. Con: It is unclear why "Islamization" - that is, the mild forms of Islamic cultural influence that will occur - is bad.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.1. Con: There have been [various](http://www.bbc.com/news/education-30129645) [cases](http://www.express.co.uk/news/uk/729512/Islamic-schools-ordered-to-shut-remain-open-amid-legal-battles) of private Islamic schools in Britain teaching radical ideologies to pupils.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.2. Con: Many people in liberal democracies find the overt misogyny symbolised in the Niqab and Burqa to be offensive with a majority wanting them banned. [yougov.co.uk](https://yougov.co.uk/news/2013/09/18/most-still-want-ban-burka-britain/)
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.2.1. Con: Only few Muslim women in high-income countries in the West actually wear these garments. According to [educated estimates](https://theconversation.com/so-few-muslim-women-wear-the-burqa-in-europe-that-banning-it-is-a-waste-of-time-82957), far less than a tenth of a percent of all Muslims - usually around 0.01% - in Western countries actually wear a burqa. Consequently, few people will encounter these garments in public.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.2.1.1. Con: Even if there are few individuals wearing them, these individuals can be seen by many, especially since Muslim populations are concentrated in large cities.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.2.1.2. Pro: Even in most supposedly more conservative countries with a Muslim majority, only [a very small minority](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2014/01/08/what-is-appropriate-attire-for-women-in-muslim-countries/) believes that women should wear Burqa and/or Niqab.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.3. Con: Local religious traditions for millennia have fought cultural war against expansion of Islam.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4. Con: Just like any other external cultural influence, an increase in Islamic influence can significantly alter the national identity of the host country.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.1. Pro: The perseverance of local culture is important to a country's identity. Losing that culture as society becomes increasingly multicultural means sacrificing an important part of what a country is, by completely changing the way the people live their lives.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.1.1. Con: Cultural differences, traditions and history would not disappear because of more tolerance.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.1.1.1. Pro: Even with an influx of immigrants, states would presumably still put a lot of funding into protecting and promoting their national traditions and heritage.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.1.1.2. Pro: Immigrants can be encouraged to participate in the traditions and heritage of their new countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.1.2. Con: Multiculturalism can integrate multiple cultures into one society without either of them encroaching on another. If that is the case, no one has to change the way they live their lives but merely to accept the ways in which others live theirs.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.1.3. Con: All cultures are and have been subject to miscegenation from others. Culture is not a result of a static society.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2. Con: Refugees increase the cultural diversity of a country, making it a more interesting place to live and allowing people to access a broader range of interactions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.1. Con: Diversity has to be weighed against other values as some influences, which could be accepted under the label of "diversity", are clearly not welcome.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.2. Pro: The areas in many cities in which immigrant or refugee populations concentrated have become ethnic enclaves and cultural as well as culinary attractions, for example [Koreatown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koreatown,_Los_Angeles) and [Little Tokyo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Little_Tokyo,_Los_Angeles) in Los Angeles, [Little Haiti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Little_Haiti) in Miami and [Greektown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greektown,_Detroit) in Detroit.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.2.1. Con: That’s not always the case. There are [areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No-go_area) in multiple cities throughout Europe in which ghettos have arisen.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3. Con: Having a diverse society is not necessarily good. Multiple cultures could cause friction and increase xenophobia among the native majority population, which is unaccustomed to foreign practices and might see refugees as a threat to their own culture.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.1. Con: Xenophobia is the real cause of friction between culturally diverse groups.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.1.1. Pro: The lower social capital and inter-personal trust that has been found in heterogeneous communities can be linked to the [prejudices of majority members](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/does-diversity-create-distrust/), e.g. Whites in America.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.1.2. Con: The fact that xenophobia is the cause is irrelevant; given that xenophobia is inevitable in the foreseeable future, it is true that increased diversity increases political friction.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.2. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.7.4.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.3. Pro: More diverse societies have [reduced support for welfare programs](http://search.proquest.com/openview/8716b95f5bc626b756228faa60b0c4f9/1?pq-origsite=gscholar&cbl=18750&diss=y), since the welfare is perceived to be going towards undeserving "outgroups."
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.4. Pro: The success of Nordic countries flows from their ability to maintain generous social programs, which in turn is enabled by their [cultural homogeneity](https://www.economist.com/blogs/freeexchange/2006/10/diversity_or_the_welfare_state).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5. Con: Increased levels of immigration tend to increase tolerance towards immigrants.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.1. Con: The refugees crisis in Italy [has increased](https://www.express.co.uk/news/world/835661/Italy-migrant-crisis-EU-Europe-borders-immigration-issue) worry and [intolerance](http://www.lastampa.it/2018/01/09/esteri/new-research-reveals-deeprooted-intolerance-for-migrants-across-italy-CPWQLoDmBwctJg0jtoeC4I/pagina.html) among [Italian](https://www.hrw.org/news/2016/07/13/dispatches-italy-wakes-xenophobia) people.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.1.1. Pro: Italy’s new Prime Minister Giuseppe Conte and his deputy Matteo Salvini have promised to put a stop to illegal immigration coming to Italy. They were elected by the Italians [to fulfill this mandate](https://www.theguardian.com/news/2018/aug/09/how-matteo-salvini-pulled-italy-to-the-far-right).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.1.2. Pro: Sicilian ports have been at [the brink](http://www.ilgiornale.it/news/cronache/sbarchi-sicilia-collasso-migranti-dirottati-nei-porti-altre-1414660.html) of collapse due to the influx of immigrants causing worry among Italian people.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.2. Con: An increased presence of migrants tends to decrease the presence of native population, thus biasing the results.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.3. Con: Sweden Democrats, an anti-immigration party is ranking the first in the polls in Sweden.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.4. Con: Switzerland has passed explicit rules [restricting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swiss_immigration_initiative,_2014) [immigration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_to_Switzerland). [Minarets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Switzerland) were also banned in 2009 since -according to Huffpost - [A majority of swiss voters](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/daniel-ammann/the-real-reasons-why-the_b_373947.html)“obviously feels that there are problems with Muslim integration into civil society at the moment.”
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.5. Con: Germany’s anti immigration party AfD has record-high poll results.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.6. Pro: In the case of [Switzerland](http://econlog.econlib.org/archives/2014/02/what_the_swiss.html), areas that experienced high levels of immigration tended to be more tolerant towards further immigration.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.6.1. Con: Switzerland has enforced [strict](https://qz.com/617050/switzerlands-largest-political-party-insists-on-depicting-foreigners-as-black-sheep/) expulsion of offending foreigners due to migration.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.6.2. Con: As with UK, areas with higher percentage of immigrants might welcome more immigrants themselves. No surprise there but that does not show a shift in the native swiss perceptions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.6.3. Con: This might be due to a selection effect: immigrants chose to go to places that were already friendly towards them.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.7. Con: Areas that experienced rapid increases in immigration were [far more likely](http://www.economist.com/news/britain/21702228-areas-lots-migrants-voted-mainly-remain-or-did-they-explaining-brexit-vote) to vote Leave in the Brexit referendum \(a decision that correlates with antipathy towards immigration\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.7.1. Con: There was a [correlation](https://theconversation.com/hard-evidence-how-areas-with-low-immigration-voted-mainly-for-brexit-62138) between voting to remain and areas with high immigration. This shows that once an area has a higher number of settled migrants, that area likely becomes more tolerant of migrants, and suggests that rapid changes in immigration is more likely the cause of intolerance.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8. Pro: Sweden and Germany, the two European countries who have accepted the most refugees, are the [only countries](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/09/16/european-opinions-of-the-refugee-crisis-in-5-charts/) in which a majority of people say that refugees "make their country stronger through their hard work and talents."
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8.1. Con: A [study](http://sverigesradio.se/sida/artikel.aspx?programid=2054&artikel=5350727) from 2012 on several European countries put Sweden as the second worst country at job market integration and in 2017 Sweden is still one of the statistically worst at [integration](https://www.ft.com/content/838d60c2-0961-11e7-97d1-5e720a26771b) of foreigners. This indicates that there exist a substantial but discrete intolerance against immigrants.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8.1.1. Con: Institutional failures of integration do not necessarily indicate intolerance towards refugees.
