1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8.2. Con: Sweden and Germany accepted more refugees precisely because of preexisting friendliness towards them. This friendliness was not caused by accepting refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8.3. Con: The 2017 German elections saw a considerable [increase in support for AfD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_federal_election,_2017), the anti-immigrant party. This is the first time a far-right party has won seats in the German Parliament since WW2, showing that many people do not agree with the idea that refugees make their country stronger.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8.3.1. Con: The AfD obtained [merely 13%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_federal_election,_2017) of the vote. All other parties back the German refugee policy \(although some with reservations\). The vast majority of Germany, thus, is not vehemently opposed to refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8.3.1.1. Con: Surveys taken during the months after the election indicate that the AFD became more popular afterwards, reaching [around 18%](https://dawum.de/Bundestag/INSA/2018-07-24/) as of July 2018.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8.4. Con: Acceptance of refugees has been decreasing in Sweden since the recent Migrant Crisis.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8.4.1. Pro: Comparing 2015 to 2017,  a [poll found that](https://www.thelocal.se/20180421/six-out-of-ten-voters-in-sweden-want-fewer-refugees-poll) the belief that "immigration had an overall positive effect on Sweden" shrank from 63 to 44 percent, while the opposite proportion, of those who said "immigration was bad for the country overall", grew from 13 to 31 percent.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.3.5.8.5. Con: At the same time, only [about a third of Swedes](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/09/16/european-opinions-of-the-refugee-crisis-in-5-charts/) and an even smaller share of Germans believe that more diversity makes their countries a better place to live. The rest believe the opposite or don't think that diversity makes a difference.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.4. Pro: [Diversity](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/how-diversity-makes-us-smarter/) makes people more economically productive and enhances creativity.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.4.1. Con: A more heterogenous society is less productive, because of miscommunication and misunderstanding between different ethnic groups.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.4.1.1. Con: Ethnic divisions are made based on arbitrary traits. Absent clear evidence of specific and disparate cultural practices between groups, the concept of ethnic heterogeneity within a population is meaningless.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.4.1.1.1. Con: These arbitrary traits seem to have a significant impact on human behavior though. Otherwise they wouldn't cause division in practically any type of community from schools, over neighborhoods, to prisons.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.4.1.1.1.1. Con: Since there is no rational basis for these divisions, there is no compelling reason to discriminate based on them. Our culture created stereotypes about the behaviors of people with certain hair colors, too, yet we would never defend policy based off of those stereotypes.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.4.1.2. Con: Ethnic groups do not communicate: individuals communicate, and most individuals in a society have absorbed enough basic social norms to be able to communicate with each other.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.4.2. Pro: A society that is culturally sensitive and empathetic towards diversity provides the building blocks to satisfy society's basic needs, right through to encouraging self-actualisation. Co-developed ideas from multicultural and multidisciplinary settings help to ensure that we are building a world that will increasingly work for everyone. Not merely for the select few.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.4.3. Pro: Racial and cultural diversity brings informational diversity - a wider range of perspectives and ideas - which enables finding more innovative solutions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.4.3.1. Con: Uneducated immigrants do not necessarily bring new useful information nor perspectives.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.5. Pro: Increased immigration increases [linguistic diversity](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/nataly-kelly/immigration-benefits_b_2523562.html) in the general population.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.5.1. Con: Language is an [important](https://www.tefl.net/elt/articles/teacher-technique/language-culture/) part of culture. Increased linguistic and cultural diversity may be threatening to local norms because of the sudden influx of alien ones.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.5.1.1. Con: A multicultural and linguistically diverse society can simply be seen as a positive evolution as opposed to a drawback and should be embraced rather than shunned.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.5.1.1.1. Con: Different cultures have different priorities. Adding different cultural viewpoints to an enterprise requires that more time and energy be devoted to synchronizing priorities and expectations.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.5.1.1.2. Pro: Working with members of another culture forces people to reexamine assumptions that their own culture takes as axiomatic.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.5.1.2. Con: Language, which is part of culture, is a constantly evolving concept. As certain aspects of language disappear, new ones appear and become part of the new cultural identity. These changes are part of languages' natural development of and are thus neither positive nor negative.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.5.1.3. Con: Preserving language for cultural value is less important than preserving lives for those in need of asylum.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.6. Con: "Interesting" is not something objective. In fact what we see is that people like to live surrounded by similar people. That's why there is places like Chinatown, Little Italy, and etc.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.6.1. Con: Ethnic enclaves like Chinatown often arise because immigrants who are unfamiliar with a new country seek out [support mechanisms](https://wol.iza.org/articles/ethnic-enclaves-and-immigrant-economic-integration/long), not necessarily because they have a longterm preference for living with people of their own ethnicity.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.7. Con: Diversity [decreases civic engagement](http://archive.boston.com/news/globe/ideas/articles/2007/08/05/the_downside_of_diversity/).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.7.1. Con: This conclusion is a one-sided representation of the underlying research. While it points out that diversity brings challenges, [the author still emphasizes](http://www.chronicle.com/blogs/percolator/robert-putnam-says-his-research-was-twisted/30357) that diversity is overall positive and "well worth the effort" of overcoming these problems.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.7.2. Con: The research underpinning this conclusion has been [called into question](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/does-diversity-create-distrust/). The reason for lower civic engagement does not necessarily lie in diversity but can also be found in prejudice, especially of Whites living among minorities.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3. Con: Robust [integration programs](https://epthinktank.eu/2017/02/08/integration-of-refugees-and-migrants-participation-in-cultural-activities/), and the participation of refugees in domestic activities, can ensure that migrants integrate in a way that is not threatening to national culture or cohesiveness.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3.1. Con: Most integration programs have failed.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3.1.1. Pro: Europe has tried - and failed - for years to integrate [Roma](http://www.dw.com/en/report-eu-failing-to-integrate-roma/a-36574818), but they still live as outsiders in most EU countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3.1.1.1. Con: Roma are an exception, since they traditionally live radically different lifestyles. The same does not hold, for example, for Syrian refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3.1.2. Pro: Speaking about Muslims in Germany, Angela Merkel previously stated that the idea of people with different cultural backgrounds living side by side has "[utterly failed](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2010/oct/17/angela-merkel-german-multiculturalism-failed)".
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3.1.2.1. Con: That quote is from 2010; Merkel's recent open-door policy to refugees indicates that she is optimistic about the future of integration efforts.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.6.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3.3. Con: Nordic countries have consistently provided non-Western immigrants with financial and educational support, yet they have formed increasingly isolated communities composed of descendants of immigrants, and no substantive integration seems to have happened. Integration programs [do not necessarily work](http://foreignpolicy.com/2016/02/10/the-death-of-the-most-generous-nation-on-earth-sweden-syria-refugee-europe/) and have struggled to effectively integrate migrants.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3.3.1. Pro: A litmus test should be used to determine whether or not immigrants can successfully assimilate.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5. Con: There have been attempts at introducing courts in high-income countries that follow [Sharia law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.1. Pro: In Britain, [Muslim arbitration tribunals](http://www.goethe.de/lhr/prj/daz/mag/igd/en9650179.htm) can make legally binding decisions if all parties agree. About 30 Sharia councils have been identified in Britain \([Bano, p. 15](https://www.reading.ac.uk/web/files/law/An_exploratory_study_of_Shariah_councils_in_England_with_respect_to_family_law_.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.1.1. Con: A study of Sharia councils in Britain concluded that the fear that they are forming a parallel legal system is unfounded. They strive to provide support in matters of religious law, not to replace the state legal system \([Bano, p. 4](https://www.reading.ac.uk/web/files/law/An_exploratory_study_of_Shariah_councils_in_England_with_respect_to_family_law_.pdf#page=15)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.1.1.1. Pro: Sharia law becomes [legally enforceable](https://fullfact.org/law/uks-sharia-courts/) only in cases such as where it is used for arbitration. In this case, all parties have to agree to using Sharia law. Even in this case, any decision reached has to obey national law.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.2. Con: In no high-income country has Sharia been introduced in a manner that ignores, replaces or supersedes ordinary law.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.1.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.3. Pro: Sharia law [can be applied](http://www.religionen-im-gespraech.de/thema/scharia-eine-gefahr-fuer-das-deutsche-recht/hintergrund/scharia-deutschland) in Germany in the form of international private law if none of the parties has German citizenship.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.3.1. Con: Nevertheless, the decisions made under Sharia law still have to [conform German laws](http://www.religionen-im-gespraech.de/thema/scharia-eine-gefahr-fuer-das-deutsche-recht/hintergrund/scharia-deutschland). Even though legal under Sharia law, decisions in favor of - for example - group marriages are therefore not legal.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.4. Con: The concept of "Sharia-Law" is too loosely defined to be considered a problem. Sharia only means "Islamic Law." Since there are a great number of Islamic branches and groups, and every branch and group has their own view of "Islamic law," Sharia is not something static and well defined.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5. Pro: Many Muslims in high-income countries would like to see Sharia law introduced there.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5.1. Pro: According to a 2006 survey, [four out of ten](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/uknews/1510866/Poll-reveals-40pc-of-Muslims-want-sharia-law-in-UK.html) British Muslims would like to see Sharia law introduced in parts of the country.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5.2. Pro: According to a 2016 survey of Germans with Turkish roots, almost half consider it more important to follow Muslim laws than to follow German laws \([WWU, p. 14](https://www.uni-muenster.de/imperia/md/content/religion_und_politik/aktuelles/2016/06_2016/studie_integration_und_religion_aus_sicht_t__rkeist__mmiger.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5.2.1. Con: The study also shows that these attitudes are receding as time passes: 57% of Turkish immigrants voiced this believe but only 36% of second- and third-generation immigrants.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5.3. Pro: A 2017 survey of Muslims in Austria found that, depending on their origin, between 10% \(Iranians\) and 36% \(Chechens\) that Islamic law should be taken into account for Muslims in Austria \([ÖIF, p. 25](http://www.heute.at/asset/original/5/9/1/591e1d09d1ea1d4e3dca8069605d28a6.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5.3.1. Con: The authors of the study emphasize that it does not live up to the standards of representativeness.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5.4. Con: Surveys also show that a majority of Muslims even in Muslim-majority countries want Sharia law to be applied [only to their kin](http://www.pewforum.org/2013/04/30/the-worlds-muslims-religion-politics-society-overview/). This indicates that they have no intention to impose Sharia law on those who do not follow Islam.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5.4.1. Con: Having the same law for all citizen is one of the bases of Western Democracies.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5.5. Pro: In France, [almost a third](https://www.ft.com/content/eaf80fce-7db5-11e6-8e50-8ec15fb462f4) of the country's Muslims consider Sharia more important than French secular law  according to a 2016 survey.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.7. Pro: Islamic perspectives and cultural practices could be incorporated into and improve national cultures.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.7.1. Con: Many cultural practices associated with Islam are most likely not attractive to the majority of citizens in high-income countries and are not welcomed there.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.7.2. Pro: Food from Islamic countries such as Kebabs from Turkey and Curry from the Indian subcontinent are very popular in European countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.7.3. Pro: Islam provides a unique perspective on [charitable giving](http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/islam/practices/zakat.shtml).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.5. Con: Other religious or ethnic groups, too, carve out their own spaces in countries and form communities. Neither is this inevitably a problem nor is it perceived as a problem in many other cases.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.5.1. Pro: In many Western cities, Koreans carve out ethnic enclaves such as the Korea-towns in [Los Angeles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koreatown,_Los_Angeles), [Toronto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koreatown,_Toronto) and [New York City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koreatown,_Manhattan).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.5.2. Pro: Mormons in the United States - where they are seen as the [most conservative](http://news.gallup.com/poll/125021/mormons-conservative-major-religious-group.aspx) of all large religious groupings - are concentrated in few areas. [Six out of ten](http://billingsgazette.com/news/state-and-regional/montana/montana-wyoming-among-states-with-highest-concentration-of-mormons/article_611a4e07-e710-5199-a748-f656dd2e15d2.html) residents in Utah consider themselves Mormons - which equals [more than two thirds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_membership_statistics_\(United_States\)) of the official membership of the Mormon church.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.6. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.2.11.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.7. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.1.8.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.11. Pro: We participate in national events, enjoy national pride, and make our nationality an essential part of our identity. Nationality is therefore morally significant to all of us.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.11.1. Con: Just because it is currently significant does not mean that it is necessary or beneficial. Identity and pride can, after all, also have other foundations than nationality, for example a regional identity or a cultural background.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.11.2. Con: Not all countries build their national pride and identity on tradition and ethnicity. Many prefer values like diversity and humanism.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.11.3. Con: Taking pride in national identity does not conflict with the adoption of new populations. An openness to refugee populations \(and to cultural exchange more generally\) can be part of a national identity of which one can be proud.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.11.4. Con: This claim is verifiably false, since it is possible to find, in every nation, at least one person who is not as described.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.12. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.13. Con: Many nations have abandoned the idea of strong national identity; for example, [Luxembourg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luxembourg). There is no reason to think that concepts of group membership or national identity are intrinsic to the concept of a state.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.14. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.1.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15. Con: National identity oftentimes takes the form of nationalism, which is problematic and not worth preserving.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.1. Pro: Participation in a national identity can lead to negative results. [Jingoism](https://www.britannica.com/topic/jingoism), a form of ultra nationalism, can lead to individuals thinking their country is always right and other countries are wrong which can lead to conflict and war.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.1.1. Con: This is an extreme form of identification with one's country which is of little relevance when debating the impact of refugees on national cultures.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2. Pro: Nationalism is a form of harmful social control, as it can shape the [collective behavior](http://bev.berkeley.edu/Ethnic%20Religious%20Conflict/Ethnic%20and%20Religious%20Conflict/2%20National%20Identity/Druckman%20nationalism.pdf) of groups. We should not let nationalism influence our policymaking decisions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1. Pro: Citizenship is an arbitrary social construct that we use to conveniently organise societies, not anything with inherent moral importance.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.1. Con: Citizenship has moral significance insofar as national identity has moral significance.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.1.1. Con: The moral responsibility inherent in being all human comes first and prevails over the moral responsibility inherent in belonging to a social group and its structures
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.1.1.1. Pro: In fact nations and social groups are historically temporary, being human will remain as long as our species exists
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.2. Con: Citizenship has a legal definition. Citizens are supposed to pay taxes. If citizenship is not considered a valid term than nothing is and that means that no argument can be valid.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.2.1. Con: This is not true: it can happen that the citizen can not pay taxes, for example because of poverty, but this condition does not deprive him of citizenship
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3. Pro: National borders are decided arbitrarily, based on the result of wars, or on geographical features. This is not a variable on which a person's standard of living should be decided.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.1. Con: The parents we are born to is equally arbitrarily decided for us yet makes a huge impact on our standard of living. the century we are born in, the geography we are born in, in the health we are born in as well as thousands of other arbitrary factors. Trying to create a world with slightly less "luck" at great cost to geopolitical stability is totally impractical and will likely cause more suffering from instability than joy from greater equality of opportunity.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.1.1. Con: This is a fallacy because a known advantage, greater equality, and a hypothetical and unquantifiable disadvantage, political instability, are compared.The first is something immediately realizable and quantifiable, the second not.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.1.1.1. Pro: We know what the results of a more open migration policy would have been. In the Mediterranean we would have saved nearly [4,000](http://www.unhcr.org/en-ie/news/latest/2016/10/580f3e684/mediterranean-death-toll-soars-2016-deadliest-year.html) lives in 2016 alone, while we can not know whether that policy would really entail greater instability or at what price.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.2. Con: Individuals have the ability to request association into other nations, and groups. The decision is not one sided, because that would be immoral. The individual has the right to ask for asylum, the group in question has the right to check to see if the individual is valuable, and safe.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3. Pro: Some national borders are not even the result of decisions made and behavior by the people living within them. The borders of many countries that today spawn refugees are the result of colonialism, imperialism and exploitation.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.1. Con: The notion of a sovereign territory is not a social construct. It exists in nature among numerous species in various forms, including \(and especially\) among our closest relatives.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.1.1. Con: The distinction between social construction and natural construction is a false problem: our brain is completely natural and naturally constructs forms of social organization. In the same way it allows us to distinguish moral problems and to legislate by going beyond the simplest forms of organization of primates closer to us
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.2. Con: There is no necessary relationship between borders and exploitation of external populations.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.3. Con: Proof by contradiction: Borders are tools of colonial and imperial exploitation. Switzerland has never been a colonial or imperial power. Therefore Switzerland does not have borders.

Clearly wrong.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.3.1. Con: The borders of Switzerland have not been determined only by Switzerland, but also by neighboring countries that have all been colonial or imperial powers
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.4. Pro: The [Sykes–Picot Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement) of 1915 between Britain and France is seen as a root cause of many sectarian conflicts that have plagued the Middle East ever since. It drew national borders [without much regard](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-36300224) to ethnic, sectarian and linguistic lines, thus paving the ground for conflict.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.4.1. Con: [No actual state borders](https://www.the-american-interest.com/2016/05/16/the-bullshistory-of-sykes-picot/) were ever drawn based on the Sykes-Picot Agreement. With the exception of demarcating the line on which the future Syrian-Iraqi border would be based, the accord had therefore [no impact at all](https://theconversation.com/obsession-with-sykes-picot-says-more-about-what-we-think-of-arabs-than-history-58775) on the region.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.4.2. Pro: The agreement is among the root causes of the ongoing [conflict between Israel and Palestinians](https://theconversation.com/the-sykes-picot-agreement-and-the-making-of-the-modern-middle-east-58780), both of which lay claim to land that they perceive as having been promised to them by colonial powers during and after World War I.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.4.3. Con: The explanation of the region's troubles via the Sykes-Picot has been labeled a "shorthand explanation" from the "realm of cliché" that ignores the complexity and the various actors and influences at play at the time \([McMeekin, p. xvii](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=bfi1CAAAQBAJ&pg=PT12&lpg=PT12&dq=%22a+shorthand+explanation+for+the+latest+upheaval+in+the+Middle+East+that+rolls+easily+off+every+tongue%22&source=bl&ots=4JdA-VbDwt&sig=JE9HQZ4vgNN0i307r1GzCKnS758&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjy14Hl8enWAhWEWrwKHYfICoIQ6AEILzAC#v=onepage&q=%22a%20shorthand%20explanation%20for%20the%20latest%20upheaval%20in%20the%20Middle%20East%20that%20rolls%20easily%20off%20every%20tongue%22&f=false)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.4.4. Con: The contemporary conflicts in the Middle East are not about and not based on national borders. They are [rooted in the authoritarian nature](http://foreignpolicy.com/2016/05/13/sykes-picot-isnt-whats-wrong-with-the-modern-middle-east-100-years/) of the region's governments and their exploitation of identity and ethnic as well as religious conflicts.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.4.4.1. Pro: [Studies indicate that](https://www.belfercenter.org/publication/getting-religion-puzzling-case-islam-and-civil-war) the link between Muslim countries and religious civil wars can be explained with their authoritarian regimes that exploit religious cleavages to increase their own legitimacy and chances for survival.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.4.4.2. Con: These conflicts may not be about national borders yet they are based problems created by these borders, for example the imposition of political boundaries irrespective of ethnic and religious differences.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.3.3.5. Con: Borders were designed to ordain a sector of control, and within that control comes the right to decide who crosses those borders. To argue that "because we have borders to potentially keep people out, we should let people in" is antithetical.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.4. Con: Morality is just as much of a societal construct as gender, race, and nationality. Where you are born heavily determines your morality.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.5. Pro: Many people have multiple citizenships; many people do not care about their citizenship; many people are citizens of countries they have never been to. Citizenship is just a legal term, not something with inherent significance.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.5.1. Con: Even if certain people don't care about citizenship, citizenship is very fundamental to the lives of many people.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.5.2. Con: Citizenship ceremonies are typically [highly emotional](http://globalnews.ca/news/3496710/emotional-ceremony-as-okanagan-immigrants-take-citizenship-oath/) and significant to people.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6. Pro: Citizenship is determined randomly and arbitrarily; for the most part, it is not something people can control. It is therefore unfair to discriminate against people on the grounds of their citizenship.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1. Con: People often premise their treatment of other individuals on circumstances beyond their control: for example, people care far more about their family members than strangers. Yet this is clearly acceptable.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1.1. Con: The fact that we traditionally behave in a certain way does not make that behavior necessarily logical or just. It is not ethical to discriminate on the basis of how close a particular person is to us.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1.2. Con: It is not clear that us caring strongly about family is a moral ground, for example: nepotism is commonly considered wrong; there are rules around judges presiding where others involved are family.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1.3. Con: The reason we owe greater duties to our family members is not that we happen to be biologically related to them, but that we form long-lasting, intimate relationships and shared experiences with them. The same cannot be said for other citizens of our country.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1.3.1. Pro: We are not meaningfully closer, or more intimately related, to another random citizen from our country than we are to a refugee or other noncitizen. So citizenship is not a valid basis for discrimination.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1.3.2. Con: Many people who have strained familial relationships still feel beholden to them. Similarly, despite lacking an established relationship, the bond of a shared culture and/or heritage still makes people feel a stronger allegiance to other members of their nation than to foreigners.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1.3.2.1. Con: Arguably, those who feel they have responsibilities towards family members who have treated them badly, or with whom they have a dysfunctional relationship, are wrong about their responsibilities.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1.3.3. Con: We share many relationships with other citizens of our country - we vote in the same elections, contribute taxes to the same government, and share a national identity. This is morally meaningful.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1.4. Pro: The communities we form with our families are analogous to the communities formed by a shared national identity. So if it is acceptable to discriminate against people who are not members of our family-community, it is therefore acceptable to discriminate against people who are not members of our nation-community.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7. Con: Citizenship indicates membership in a political community and participation in a national identity. These things are morally meaningful.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.1. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.2. Con: These political communities are themselves artificially created, and arbitrarily exclude certain groups. They do not provide support for the inherent importance of citizenship.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.2.1. Con: All identities and communities are artificial and arbitrarily exclude some people. This does not rob them of moral significance.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3. Con: The similarities between people due to their shared humanity run far deeper than relatively superficial differences based on national membership or traditions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1. Con: Recognition of basic humanity does not resolve genuine differences in ideology, religion or philosophy reflected in national identity.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.1. Con: Recognition of our basic common humanity triggers regions of the brain associated with compassion.  Compassion does resolve ideological differences on the basis of common relation \([Stevens/Woodruff, Chapter 4](https://www.amazon.com/Neuroscience-Empathy-Compassion-Self-Compassion/dp/0128098376/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1504814398&sr=8-1&keywords=The+Neuroscience+of+Empathy%2C+Compassion%2C+and+Self-Compassion)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.2. Con: The areas of the brain that react to compassion have nothing to do with the argument and should be eliminated.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.3. Pro: Compassion does nothing to resolve ideological differences as they are by definition not part of our commonality. Soldiers and who fight each other recognize their commonality. We know this from what they say when they meet each other after the war. Nonetheless they are quite good at killing each other.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.4. Pro: The Muslim Quran and Hadith texts require non-Muslims to either convert or pay the jizya and become subordinate to Muslims. This would place them under Sharia law.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.4.1. Pro: In verses like [9:29](https://quran.com/9/29), the Quran explicitly calls upon Muslims to fight non-believers until they subordinate to Islam and pay the Jizya.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.4.1.1. Con: The verse has received [various interpretations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/At-Tawba_29), some of which stress that it is by no means a universal condemnation of non-Muslims but specific to its context: Muhammad's military campaign [against Tabouk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expedition_to_Tabouk) and its citizens.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.4.2. Con: Not all Muslims ascribe to traditional and literal ways of interpreting their holy scriptures.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.4.2.1. Pro: In Germany, two thirds of Muslims disagree with the idea that Muslims should follow the Quran literally and slightly more than half disagree with the statement that good Muslims should attempt to convert non-believers \([BMI, p. 118](https://www.deutsche-islam-konferenz.de/SharedDocs/Anlagen/DIK/DE/Downloads/WissenschaftPublikationen/muslime-in-deutschland-lang-dik.pdf?__blob=publicationFile)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.4.2.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.3.3.2.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.1.4.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.5.5.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.3.2. Pro: Of all the important characteristics that are fundamental to our lives - things like our capacity for language, creation, social interaction - almost all are universal to all of humanity. The human characteristics which differ across cultures are a tiny subset of the much deeper similarities that all humans possess.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.5.2.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.5. Con: Even if citizenship signifies an important community, then high-income countries should welcome more people into that community to grow its size, rather than exclude people.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.7.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.1.6.1.3.3.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.2. Pro: Nationalism is [a harmful form of patriotism](https://plato.stanford.edu/entries/patriotism/#PatNat). While patriotism is a devotion to a particular place and a way of life one thinks best, but has no wish to impose on others, nationalism is accordingly aggressive.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.1.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.2.2. Con: This is a sweeping overgeneralization. There are multiple forms of nationalism; and while some might tend more towards aggression or intolerance, others do not.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.2.2.1. Pro: Although the exclusive nature of [ethnic nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_nationalism) tends to be more harmful, [civic nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civic_nationalism) is far more inclusive since its membership is voluntary and revolves around shared social values rather than shared heritage. This type of nationalism is thus less likely to be harmful or xenophobic as it is compatible with progressive values like freedom, equality, and tolerance.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.2.2.2. Pro: [Sports nationalism](http://www.washingtonexaminer.com/nationalism-is-not-necessarily-a-bad-thing/article/2599075), best illustrated by the Olympic games, is another example of nationalism that has positive attributes. Not only does it easily embrace ethnic and racial diversity, but it offers an opportunity for people from nations suffering political or economic divides to unite in celebration of their fellow countrymen's athletic prowess.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.2.2.3. Con: The forms of nationalism that do not tend toward aggression and intolerance, however, are generally the ones that do not see refugees as a threat to their national identity and would see new cultures in their country as enriching rather than eroding their heritage.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.2.3. Con: Nationalism is not necessarily a bad thing, as the shared sense of norms, mores, and identity that it gives citizens not only strengthens communities but helps to prevent feelings of isolation and anomie.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.3. Con: Even if nationalism is bad, that does not mean we should not acknowledge its existence, and the importance of national identity to the lives of many people.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.4. Con: The fact that nationalism can shape collective behaviour does not make it bad. Shaping collective behaviour can be very good if it makes people more cooperative and willing to help each other, as nationalism has the potential to do.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.3. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.15.2.2.3.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.16. Con: Many nations premise their national identity on diversity and inclusivity: for example, [Sweden](http://foreignpolicy.com/2016/02/10/the-death-of-the-most-generous-nation-on-earth-sweden-syria-refugee-europe/), [America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_Colossus), and [Canada](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/donald-trump-justin-trudeau-canada-immigration-ban-muslim-countries-a7552186.html).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.16.1. Con: If certain countries premise their national identity on inclusivity, then they ought to take in refugees. However, other countries do not, and those countries should not be obligated to erode their national identities.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.17. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.2.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.18. Con: National identities can, and do, evolve as a country's population changes. This cultural evolution is perfectly natural, and nothing to be afraid of.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.18.1. Con: When Central \([V4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group)\) Europeans compare relative security and [conflictlessness](http://www.national-geographic.cz/clanky/svetovy-index-miru-ceska-republika-je-sestou-nejbezpecnejsi-zemi-sveta-20160620.html) of their countries with France, Britain, Germany and Sweden, they [often reach conclusion](https://cs.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evropsk%C3%A1_migra%C4%8Dn%C3%AD_krize#cite_note-176) that they do not want their national culture [to evolve as it did](http://www.deniklegie.cz/domains/deniklegie.cz/index.php/politika/2313-politika-v-cele-evrope-se-prizpusobuje-populistickym-floskulim) in aforementioned countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.18.2. Pro: The US now has a [very high proportion](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2015/jun/29/us-second-biggest-spanish-speaking-country) of Spanish-speakers. This is reflected in changes in national culture: the increased successes of [Spanish-language songs](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/despacito-is-the-first-spanish-language-song-to-be-1-in-the-us-since-the-macarena_us_591dab8fe4b03b485caf3b29), [bilingual schools](http://www.nbcnews.com/news/latino/spanish-language-immersion-schools-gain-popularity-n225776), even the popularity of Mexican-American [food](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burrito).
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.18.3. Pro: German immigrants to the US [introduced](https://www.economist.com/news/united-states/21642222-americas-largest-ethnic-group-has-assimilated-so-well-people-barely-notice-it) Christmas trees, the Easter bunny, pretzels, and hot dogs, all of which are staples of modern American culture.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.18.3.1. Con: National identities are open to fairly meaningless things like hot dogs and trees. It is the meaningful aspects of National Identity that people fear losing: democracy; equality of women; tolerance; policing by consent; secularism and reformed religion; permissiveness.
1.1.6.5.1.4.1.19. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.1.10.3.1.4.4.3.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2. Con: Accepting refugees can be a [solution](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-sweden-immigration-idUSKBN14B1OK) to the problem of aging populations.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.1. Con: Accepting large amounts of refugees to balance out an ageing population risks changing the demographics of the country considerably, and harming social cohesion.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.2. Con: This is classic Ponzinomics. Increasing the population in order to deal with an aging population only serves to create an even larger population. In a few decades the immigrant population will have got old thus necessitating an even larger influx of new immigrants. Etcetera ad infinitum!
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.2.1. Con: Immigrants tend to be [more](https://www.econstor.eu/bitstream/10419/71734/1/73974254X.pdf) [fertile](https://qz.com/811195/immigrants-helped-bump-germanys-fertility-rate-to-its-highest-in-33-years/) than the native population, so they offer a more lasting solution to demographic crises.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.2.1.1. Con: As studies from [France](https://www.demographic-research.org/volumes/vol36/45/) and the [United States](http://www.ppic.org/content/pubs/rb/RB_402LHRB.pdf) show, the fertility rates of most immigrant populations decline over generations and converge with a country's patterns.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.2.2. Con: The solution to demographic crises is, indeed, for countries with low fertility to continuously accept young migrants. This is not a conclusion to be avoided.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.3. Pro: High income countries tend to have low birthrates, often leading to aging and shrinking populations \(e.g. Japan\). Low income countries tend to have higher birthrates, leading to a population surplus. It makes economic sense to balance those aging populations in richer economies by taking in young workers from countries with growing populations.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.3.1. Con: Current uses of this model create extractive practices. In most cases, immigrant workers are subject to low-paying, low-benefit, dangerous work \(like many jobs in agribusinesses, mining, chemical etc. and with few exceptions in tech and medicine\). The native population benefits from their hard work, but the immigrant worker has often has their health and wellness taken from them and remains a lower-class citizen.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.3.2. Con: This model would perhaps help under normal circumstances, however in this circumstances, refugees come from a large range of demographics including the elderly and middle aged. Not necessarily 'young workers' as the claim suggests.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.4. Con: It will artificially inflate the job market in times where automatization and huge job loss are just around the corner.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.5. Con: Only if they actually worked, but since about [81%](http://www.handelsblatt.com/politik/deutschland/bundesagentur-fuer-arbeit-knapp-jeder-fuenfte-asylbewerber-hat-berufs-oder-studienabschluss/12444994.html) of German refugees have no formal qualification at all, it's more likely that they will live on welfare themselves.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.5.1. Con: As the German Federal Agency for Work [emphasizes](https://www.handelsblatt.com/politik/deutschland/bundesagentur-fuer-arbeit-knapp-jeder-fuenfte-asylbewerber-hat-berufs-oder-studienabschluss/12444994.html), these numbers are not representative. They are based on voluntary surveys and classify people as not having a formal education who cannot provide proof for it. Naturally, this is the case for some refugees who do not have documents.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.6. Con: Immigration does not solve the problem of aging population, it simply changes the existing population with another. In fact it hides the demographic problem itself by giving the false impression of population growth.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7. Pro: If refugees are allowed to work and contribute to social services through the taxes they pay, they will effectively finance the aging native population's healthcare and pensions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.1. Con: Refugees will put an additional burden on the struggling pension schemes of high-income countries once they age.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.1.1. Con: In the [UK](https://www.litrg.org.uk/tax-guides/migrants-and-tax/national-insurance-migrants/national-insurance-and-uk-state-pension) and [USA](https://www.elderlawanswers.com/who-is-eligible-for-social-security-retirement-benefits-12052) the state pension is contributory, meaning refugees \(or any migrants\) are not eligible unless they have been working for 10 years.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.1.1.1. Pro: By the time these refugees are eligible for a pension, they will on average be [contributing more than they cost](https://www.kialo.com/should-high-income-countries-take-in-refugees-2214/2214.0=2214.1-2214.1493-2214.471+2214.478-2214.3730-2214.3856/-2214.3856).
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.1.1.2. Pro: In the UK the full amount is not payable unless they have been working 35 years.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.1.2. Con: As the population of high-income countries are aging rapidly, the influx of [mostly young refugees](https://www.weforum.org/agenda/2015/10/can-refugees-revive-europes-ageing-population/) has the potential to improve the ratio of those paying into pension schemes and those receiving pensions, thus improving the pension situation in the long term.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2. Pro: There is evidence that refugees may be net fiscal contributors.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.1. Pro: In the U.S., while it costs approximately $15,000 to settle a refugee, and the Federal government pays out an approximate further $92,000 in welfare benefits over the first 20 years of a refugees stay, it is estimated that the Federal government gets back [$129,000 in taxes](http://www.businessinsider.com/how-much-do-refugees-cost-us-taxpayers-2017-6) over those 20 years. So there is a net gain of about $22,000, for the Federal government when it comes to refugees who stay long-term.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.1.1. Con: This net gain disappears once[inflation](https://smartasset.com/investing/inflation-calculator#xbHmVoBM2z) is taken into account. $15,000 \(to settle the refugee\) would be worth approx. $22,000 20 years later. $92,000 over the first years of a refugees stay would be worth approx 111,000 only ten years later. The government could lose about $26,000 due to inflation variance, for a total net loss of $4,000.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.1.1.1. Con: It is likely that many long-term refugees will[become citizens](http://www.sctimes.com/story/news/local/immigration/2015/10/14/fact-check-refugees-can-become-us-citizens/73932826/) or continue to stay, which means the government will continue to receive monetary benefit from taxes without paying further welfare.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.1.2. Pro: This part of the study only looked at adults \(18-45\).
If children were taken into account, the net gain over 20 years would be much higher, as the study shows child refugees attain better economic outcomes than adults.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.1.3. Con: This neglects to count future pension costs of the refugee. The government may begin to make a loss as refugees retire.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.2. Pro: [In America](http://www8.nationalacademies.org/onpinews/newsitem.aspx?RecordID=23550), immigrants are net fiscal contributors on the federal level \(though this is not true at the state and local level\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.3. Pro: A 20 year US study found [no difference in economic outcomes](http://www.nber.org/digest/aug17/w23498.shtml) between refugees who arrived as children and U.S.-born citizens.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.4. Pro: Migrants and asylum seekers can benefit the economies of their host nations. As [shown](http://advances.sciencemag.org/content/4/6/eaaq0883) in the data analysis of 30 years of data from 15 countries in Western Europe, migrants positively affect the economy within a year of arrival, continuing to have significant impact for 2+ years. Asylum seekers have a significant impact after 3-7 years since arrival, but it is not as strong an impact as that of other migrant groups.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.8. Pro: Germany's demographic projections are much better after the refugee crisis as [studies sugges](https://www.weforum.org/agenda/2017/04/population-ageing-and-immigration-germanys-demographic-question)t the influx of people will help keep the population number stable for the next decades.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.8.1. Con: As many refugees will not receive German citizenship, these aren't necessarily the demographic prospects of the German people.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.8.1.1. Con: If the demographic prospects of the people living in Germany improve, this automatically means that those of Germans improve as most Germans live in Germany.
1.1.6.5.1.4.2.8.1.1.1. Con: The prospects of the local german population do not improve with inmigration. The demographics of ethnic germans stay the same.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3. Pro: Taking in refugees with low education will make them competitors on the marketplace to other people with low education. Following the [law of supply and demand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supply_and_demand) this will increase the supply of low educated workers and therefore decrease the price of their labor.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.1. Con: Many refugees, as temporary residents, will not have the permits necessary to work legally, and therefore will not be active on the job market.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.2. Con: A slight decline in wages for low-educated workers in a high-income country is acceptable, because their lives are still more secure and materially better than the life of a refugee in an unstable, war-torn country.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.3. Con: This is the [lump of labour fallacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lump_of_labour_fallacy). When new workers enter a marketplace, the supply of jobs does not remain constant. Rather, the consumption of the new workers creates new jobs, meaning that the price of labour does not necessarily decrease.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.3.1. Con: The quality of the immigrant workforce is the determining factor in what impact they will have on the economy and the availability of jobs. In the same wiki you quote on "lump of labour fallacy" it says, "skilled immigrating workers can bring capabilities that are not available in the native workforce."  In the claim above yours, the poster specifies  low educated immigrants.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.3.1.1. Con: The [available](http://www.hbs.edu/faculty/Publication%20Files/09-013_15702a45-fbc3-44d7-be52-477123ee58d0.pdf) [research](http://davidcard.berkeley.edu/papers/card-peri-jel-april-6-2016.pdf) [indicates](http://davidcard.berkeley.edu/papers/mariel-impact.pdf) [that](http://www.apdr.pt/siteRPER/numeros/RPER24/24.1.pdf) entry of workers, even low-skilled ones, tends to have only [small](http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/001979398704000305) and temporary impacts on native wages and employment, if any.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.3.1.1.1. Con: Immigrants are not necessarily analogous to refugees in this respect. Most immigrants are accepted specifically for the purpose of having them work, and many have obtained jobs prior to arrival. Refugees are accepted for humanitarian reasons, and therefore their patterns of employment may differ.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.3.1.1.2. Pro: Refugees are a subset of all migrants. The moral imperative for taking them in does not diminish the [economic benefits](https://www.newscientist.com/article/mg22730383-800-why-welcoming-more-refugees-makes-economic-sense-for-europe/) that they bring.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.3.1.1.2.1. Con: The more recent numbers suggest that only a [quarter to a third of the newcomers](https://www.express.co.uk/news/world/820480/Germany-migrant-crisis-refugees-long-term-unemployment-benefits-Angela-Merkel) would enter the labour market over the next five years.
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.3.1.1.3. Con: The evidence is mixed, and there is strong evidence for the proposition that low-skilled migration [hurts domestic workers](http://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2016/09/trump-clinton-immigration-economy-unemployment-jobs-214216).
1.1.6.5.1.4.3.3.1.1.3.1. Con: There is not "strong" evidence that immigration hurts domestic workers. There are a few [outlier studies](https://www.economist.com/blogs/freeexchange/2017/06/immigration-economics), including by the cited source, that show there may be a negative impact for some groups where there is no redistribution, and only in some countries. Pretty much all studies of immigration show an overall positive impact to the economy. For example [this by OECD](https://www.google.co.uk/url?sa=t&source=web&rct=j&url=https://www.oecd.org/migration/OECD%2520Migration%2520Policy%2520Debates%2520Numero%25202.pdf&ved=2ahUKEwjB3qmGmN3YAhXFJ1AKHfiRAsgQFjACegQIExAB&usg=AOvVaw2ImcGaSyQizrZG1DpCv85L) and [this literature review](https://www.google.co.uk/url?sa=t&source=web&rct=j&url=http://www.hbs.edu/faculty/Publication%2520Files/09-013_15702a45-fbc3-44d7-be52-477123ee58d0.pdf&ved=2ahUKEwiP9NyfnN3YAhVFPVAKHUCaDMgQFjAAegQIERAB&usg=AOvVaw1jGWzeaAztMsQ0BUTRhLVw) from Harvard.
1.1.6.5.1.4.4. Con: Social programmes give those people purchasing power who are [likely to spend the whole amount of money](https://www.financialsamurai.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/savings-rates-by-wealth-class.png) \(income\) which would be an economic stimulus.
1.1.6.5.1.4.4.1. Con: Or they could send the money to their family in their home country and effectively steal from the economy of their host countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.4.2. Con: Social programmes could instead be spent on existing low-income citizens of the high-income country, which would provide an equivalent economic stimulus.
1.1.6.5.1.4.5. Pro: Taking in refugees costs a lot of money.
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.1. Pro: Dividing the expenditure of rich countries on refugee issues by the number of arrivals yields costs of about 17.000€ per person in Germany and 37.000€ in Sweden \([OECD, p.2](https://www.oecd.org/els/mig/migration-policy-debates-13.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.2. Pro: Across OECD countries, the costs of accommodating and processing asylum seekers in their first year after arrival alone are estimated to be around 10.000€ per person - and possibly much higher \([OECD, p. 1](https://www.oecd.org/els/mig/migration-policy-debates-13.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.2.1. Con: At the same time, the [paper](https://www.oecd.org/els/mig/migration-policy-debates-13.pdf) cautions that "annual costs decline considerably in the following years".
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.3. Pro: Unless the average productivity of refugees was at least equal to the average productivity of existing residents, accepting refugees would also lower average productivity and living standards.
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.3.1. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.3.
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.4. Con: The cost of hosting refugees decreases significantly the longer they stay. Consider Sweden: the annual spending per refugees goes down by about 70% within seven years \([OECD, p. 6](https://www.oecd.org/els/mig/migration-policy-debates-13.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.5. Pro: These costs are born by the citizens of high-income countries without any clear justification. They pay for something they are not responsible for.
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.6. Pro: Germany, for example, spent [$20bn](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/germany-refugees-spend-20-billion-euros-2016-angela-merkel-crisis-budgets-middle-east-north-africa-a7623466.html) on refugees in 2016. This is only [slightly more](https://www.bundesfinanzministerium.de/Content/EN/Bilderstrecken/Media_Centre/Graphics/infograpfics-2017-federal-budget.html?notFirst=true&docId=94868) than all spending on research and education.
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.6.1. Con: These numbers have to be seen in context. In the case of Germany, the government nevertheless had a budget surplus in 2016 [of €6.2bn](https://www.reuters.com/article/germany-budget-idUSB4N18L02A).
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.6.1.1. Con: It's not really that Germany has money to waste. [Infrastructure](https://www.cnbc.com/2016/09/14/germany-has-a-crumbling-infrastructure-problem.html), for example, is struggling to maintain current levels despite a massive spending program.
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.6.2. Con: Germany is an exceptional case as it took in a large number of refugees in 2015 and 2016. If these would have been distributed more equally over European countries, the German expenses would have been much lower.
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.6.2.1. Con: Germany wasn't the only country to pick up a disproportionate amount of refugees. The refugee placement throughout the entire of Europe has been sporadic.
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.6.3. Con: Whereas those $20 billion represent 5.8% of Germany's [federal budget](http://www.dw.com/en/german-federal-budget-goes-up-for-2017/a-36528845), they are a mere 0.5% of America's [federal budget](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_United_States_federal_budget). The relevance of these costs therefore depends on the context
1.1.6.5.1.4.5.7. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.2.7.2.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6. Pro: Taking in large groups of refugees can lead to increased ethnic tensions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.1. Pro: Antisemitism is common among refugees and poses a threat to Jewish populations.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.1.1. Pro: According to a study among refugees in one German state, more than half of those from Syria, Iraq and Afghanistan believe that Jews have too much influence in the world. This attitude is independent of age, education and the degree of religiosity \([HSS, p. 68](https://www.hss.de/download/publications/Asylsuchende_in_Bayern.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.1.1.1. Con: This attitude does not necessarily translate into hostile behavior. Around 90% of refugees surveyed in this study stated that people deserve the same respect independent of whether they are religious or not \([HSS, p. 70](https://www.hss.de/download/publications/Asylsuchende_in_Bayern.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.1.2. Pro: Many refugees are young Muslims. According to a survey of young Muslims in Germany, a quarter of them blame Israel alone for the Middle East conflict and believe that Jews should leave the region. Among non-Muslims, only 5% hold these attitudes \([BMI, p. 77](https://www.bmi.bund.de/SharedDocs/downloads/DE/publikationen/2017/expertenbericht-antisemitismus-in-deutschland.pdf?__blob=publicationFile)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.1.3. Con: The Antisemitism of refugees has to be seen in context. In Germany, around 90% of antisemitic crimes were committed by right-wing actors during the past couple of years; very few were committed by foreigners \([BMI, p. 39](https://www.bmi.bund.de/SharedDocs/downloads/DE/publikationen/2017/expertenbericht-antisemitismus-in-deutschland.pdf?__blob=publicationFile)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.1.3.1. Con: The same report cautions that interviews with victims of Antisemitic crimes report that Muslims are by far the most common perpetrators. A plausible explanation for this discrepancy has so far not been found \([BMI, p. 39](https://www.bmi.bund.de/SharedDocs/downloads/DE/publikationen/2017/expertenbericht-antisemitismus-in-deutschland.pdf?__blob=publicationFile)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.1.4. Con: Attitudes do not necessarily translate into actions. The number of antisemitic crimes has been relatively stable for years and saw a decrease - not an increase - in 2015, when Germany began to take in many refugees \([BMI, p. 39](https://www.bmi.bund.de/SharedDocs/downloads/DE/publikationen/2017/expertenbericht-antisemitismus-in-deutschland.pdf?__blob=publicationFile)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.2. Pro: The increasing amount of beggars in Sweden has created hostility towards [Roma](https://www.irishtimes.com/news/world/europe/sweden-s-tolerant-image-compromised-by-attacks-on-roma-1.2311689) within the Swedish society.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.3. Pro: The rise of [Islamophobia](http://www.mei.edu/content/article/europe-s-islamophobia-and-refugee-crisis) in Europe is tied to the refugee crisis.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.3.1. Con: Rejecting refugees due to the rise of Islamophobia in the West equals capitulation in the face of irrational and misguided prejudices.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.3.1.1. Con: You have to consider the impact of any policy in the real world and not in some idealised version of it.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.3.2. Con: Correlation is not causation. In the UK, groups such as UKIP, Britain First and the Conservatives have also been accused of stoking Islamophobia, and hate crimes increased significantly after the Brexit vote.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.3.3. Con: This may be due to the increased media attention and public debate, rather than a direct effect of more people living with refugees/migrants.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.4. Con: Getting to know people of different backgrounds by taking in refugees can inspire more nuanced ideas about both the people encountered and different cultures in general, leading to decreased ethnic tensions.
1.1.6.5.1.4.6.5. Con: Social segregation in diverse societies causes the rise of ethnic tensions. See[Eric Uslaner - Segregation and Mistrust](https://books.google.dk/books/about/Segregation_and_Mistrust.html?id=Et_tuQAACAAJ&redir_esc=y&hl=en)
1.1.6.5.1.4.7. Con: The human cost of not taking in refugees - leaving them in limbo in refugee camps - is greater than the consequences of accepting them. The costs that wealthy countries incur are also minimal relative to what the refugees themselves have suffered and lost, and minimal relative to the costs incurred by [poorer countries](http://www.unhcr.org/news/latest/2017/2/58b001ab4/poorer-countries-host-forcibly-displaced-report-shows.html) where most refugees are currently trapped.
1.1.6.5.1.4.8. Con: If the amount of refugees is fairly shared between high-income countries, their taking in is highly manageable for these countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.9. Pro: Taking in some refugees from some conflicts but not others shows an international bias that may lead to negative diplomatic impact and showcase the country hosting the refugees in a bad light.
1.1.6.5.1.4.9.1. Con: There is no historical precedent for a negative effect of taking in refugees \(in a not obviously discriminatory manner\) on a country's reputation.
1.1.6.5.1.4.9.2. Pro: Awarding asylum to some refugees and not others is inherently unfair, unjust and inefficient. Only a relatively small percentage of asylum seekers \(the lottery winners\) can be accomodated and sufficiently integrated \(vs. the millions of lottery losers\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.10. Pro: Taking in a significant share of the world's refugees would significantly alter the population structure of high-income countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.10.1. Pro: According to the UN, there are about [22.5 Million](http://www.unhcr.org/figures-at-a-glance.html) registered refugees at the moment and many more displaced people. If they would all show up at the borders of the European Union, they would constitute 4% of the bloc's population.
1.1.6.5.1.4.11. Con: It's unlikely that refugees would stay in their host country if they are given the chance to return home absent the thing that made them flee in the first place.
1.1.6.5.1.4.11.1. Con: Definitions of the term "refugee", for example [by the United Nations](http://www.unrefugees.org/what-is-a-refugee/), usually do contain any reference to an individual's interest or will to return home. While this may be the case for some individuals, this should therefore not be assumed to be true for all refugees.
1.1.6.5.1.4.11.1.1. Con: They are certainly unable or unwilling to return to their home country during the period\(s\) of conflict, but this is not the same that stating they will remain unable or unwilling if the situation in their country stabilises.
1.1.6.5.1.4.11.2. Con: According to surveys among Syrian refugees in camps in Jordan and Lebanon, only about four out of ten consider it likely that they will permanently return home \([ASDA'A Burson-Marsteller, p. 7](http://arabyouthsurvey.com/syrian-refugees/pdf/AYS%202017_Syrian%20Refugee%20Whitepaper%20English%20300717.pdf)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.11.2.1. Pro: The share of refugees who shows a desire to return home is likely to be even lower once they arrive in high-income countries where they can most likely can expect a better future than in refugee camps.
1.1.6.5.1.4.11.3. Con: According to a 2014 study among refugees in Germany, 85% want to permanently reside in the country and 80% want to obtain German citizenship \([BAMF, p. 10](http://www.bamf.de/SharedDocs/Anlagen/EN/Downloads/Infothek/Forschung/Forschungsberichte/fb28-fluechtlingsstudie2014-kurzfassung.pdf?__blob=publicationFile)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.11.3.1. Pro: In addition, those who did not say that they want to remain permanently in Germany usually stated that they "don't know". Virtually none of the refugees who participated in the study showcased any plans to leave \([BAMF, p. 269](http://www.bamf.de/SharedDocs/Anlagen/DE/Publikationen/Forschungsberichte/fb28-fluechtlingsstudie-2014.pdf?__blob=publicationFile)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.11.3.2. Pro: If not only those are counted who definitely want to obtain German citizenship but also those who "probably" want to do so, more than 90% of refugees indicate the desire to become German \([BAMF, p. 271](http://www.bamf.de/SharedDocs/Anlagen/DE/Publikationen/Forschungsberichte/fb28-fluechtlingsstudie-2014.pdf?__blob=publicationFile)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.12. Pro: Culture shapes society. Culture is the main reason for income differences between societies. Many high-inome countries already deal with parallel societies and their income diferences.
1.1.6.5.1.4.12.1. Pro: One of the reasons for Europe's early rise lies in the emergence of capitalism and the progress that went hand in hand with it. This, in return, can be traced back to a protestant mindset and the value placed on secular work and the pursuit of economic gain, as [Max Weber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Protestant_Ethic_and_the_Spirit_of_Capitalism) famously argued.
1.1.6.5.1.4.12.2. Pro: Having a culture based on strong work ethics and solid entrepreneurial spirit can ensure that low-income countries can accumulate enough wealth to become high-income countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.12.3. Pro: Among the reasons that have been cited for China's inability to keep up with the West's industrial revolution are "failures of imperial will and oversight, of bureaucratic morale and initiative, and of corruption and maladministration" \([Rowe, p. 153](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=KN7Awmzx2PAC&pg=PA150&lpg=PA150&dq=%22a+perfect+storm+of+three+simultaneous+problems:+the+external+shock+of+the+expanding+West,+a+secular+crisis+caused+by+an+accumulation+of+socioeconomic+difficulties+over+the+long+term+and+more+acute+political+dysfunctions+associated+with+the+familiar+pattern+of+the+dynastic+cycle%22&source=bl&ots=DoyTNTvNWL&sig=eABmvt-ADcuJNf_eU_zQwHjFxvA&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjM5Y_3_NPZAhVTNrwKHVqpBbUQ6AEIJzAA#v=onepage&q=%22a%20perfect%20storm%20of%20three%20simultaneous%20problems%3A%20the%20external%20shock%20of%20the%20expanding%20West%2C%20a%20secular%20crisis%20caused%20by%20an%20accumulation%20of%20socioeconomic%20difficulties%20over%20the%20long%20term%20and%20more%20acute%20political%20dysfunctions%20associated%20with%20the%20familiar%20pattern%20of%20the%20dynastic%20cycle%22&f=false)\).
1.1.6.5.1.4.13. Pro: Taking in refugees might motivate many others to follow them, especially if they are likely to receive asylum. This could quickly overwhelm the capacities of high-income countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.1. Pro: There are currently more than [22 Million](http://www.unhcr.org/figures-at-a-glance.html) refugees worldwide and over 60 Million forcibly displaced people. If they were all to aspire refuge in high-income countries, this would quickly overwhelm them.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.2. Pro: More than quarter of the world's displaced people are currently in [the Middle East and North Africa](http://www.unhcr.org/figures-at-a-glance.html). This puts them in proximity to Europe's high-income countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.3. Con: Even though high-income countries have taken in millions, about [85%](https://www.weforum.org/agenda/2017/06/eighty-four-percent-of-refugees-live-in-developing-countries/) of the world's refugees are in developing countries. Among the [ten countries](https://www.weforum.org/agenda/2017/06/eighty-four-percent-of-refugees-live-in-developing-countries/) hosting the most refugees, only a single one is rich. This indicates that most refugees can't or don't want to head to high-income countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.4. Con: The [World Bank](http://databank.worldbank.org/data/download/site-content/CLASS.xls) classifies 77 countries as High income, the [UNHCR](http://www.unhcr.org/figures-at-a-glance.html) counts 22.5 million refugees, and the total population of the HI countries combined is 1.2 billion. If the 22.5 million refugees are divided among the High Income countries, where the share is proportional to each countries population, the percentage each share of refugees would be 1.8% out of each country's total population, which is highly manageable.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.4.1. Con: As of late 2016, Germany had a population of [82.5 Million](https://www.destatis.de/DE/PresseService/Presse/Pressemitteilungen/2018/01/PD18_019_12411.html) people and had taken in [1.6 Million](https://www.destatis.de/DE/PresseService/Presse/Pressemitteilungen/2017/11/PD17_387_12521.html) refugees. The share of refugees therefore stood at 1.9%. Although Germany is among the world's richest nations, this inflow proved problematic and highly controversial.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.4.1.1. Pro: In Germany, [the right-wing Alternative for Germany](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-37274201) won 13% of the vote in the [2017 national election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_federal_election,_2017), running mostly on a platform against migration and Muslim influences. In the previous election it won less than 5% of votes.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.4.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.5.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.4.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.7.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.4.2. Con: Even if all high-income countries would suddenly agree to take in "significant numbers" of refugees, it is highly unrealistic to expect that they'd take in refugees representing 1.8% of their population.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.4.2.1. Pro: Some countries already refuse to take in "significant" numbers of refugees and would certainly not host 1.8% of their population. Case in point: [Japan](https://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/2017/06/lives-limbo-japan-accepts-refugees-170608122312650.html) which accepts less than 1% of asylum applications, even in the current era of refugee crisis, and took in only 700 refugees in the last 35 years.
1.1.6.5.1.4.13.4.3. Con: This does not take into account changes in numbers caused by the changed incentives. If high-income countries pledged to take in and subsidize refugees, more people from regions in crisis would choose to become refugees instead of trying to hold out in their home countries.
1.1.6.5.1.4.14. Con: Taking in refugees consumes goodwill and might erode support for other humanitarian actions, such as development aid and/or humanitarian intervention.
1.1.6.5.1.4.14.1. Con: After failures of previous interventions such as in [Libya](https://www.foreignaffairs.com/articles/libya/obamas-libya-debacle) as well as protracted wars in Afghanistan and Iraq, there is no hunger among the people of high-income countries for more military interventions abroad anyway.
1.1.6.5.2. Pro: Individuals have no duty to provide other citizens with welfare benefits, but the state does. So a state clearly has stronger duties to its own citizens than individuals do.
1.1.6.5.3. Pro: The very nature of a political community is such that members of that community must be free to self-determine and associate with whom they choose; this means being able to exclude whoever they choose.
1.1.6.5.3.1. Con: Accepting refugees is in the direct self-interest of high-income countries; so in any case their self-determination, which is based on the democratic mandate to do the best they can for their citizens, implies that they should take in refugees.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1. Pro: Accepting refugees benefits the citizens of high-income countries.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.1. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.5.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.2. Con: If there is a moral obligation to accept refugees, it wouldn't matter whether or not accepting refugees is beneficial.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.2.1. Con: It matters because all countries have a moral obligation to make life better for their citizens.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.2.1.1. Con: That's a different obligation. If taking in refugees is better for citizens, that doesn't necessarily mean there is a moral obligation to take in refugees. If taking in refugees was not beneficial to citizens, the moral obligation to citizens would still exist, but would involve rejecting refugees.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.2.1.2. Pro: The idea that countries have an obligation to their citizens over people from other countries may be established by precedent, however this is based on morally dubious grounds: basing a person's worth on the arbitrary place of birth.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.2.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.4. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.2.1.1.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5. Con: Taking in refugees harms native workers.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.1. Con: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.3.3.1.1.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.2. Pro: [When surveyed](http://www.igmchicago.org/surveys/low-skilled-immigrants), a majority of economists agree that low-skilled immigration helps the average American, but also agree that it hurts worse-off, lower-skilled Americans.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3. Con: Many of the refugees do [ungrateful and low paid jobs](http://www.dw.com/en/economist-geis-33000-jobs-for-refugees-a-success/a-19397020), which citizens of high-income countries refuse or do not want to do. It is a common mistake to claim that refugees steal jobs.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3.1. Con: Even these ungrateful and low-paid jobs could otherwise be done by natives.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3.2. Pro: A [2014 Study](https://wol.iza.org/uploads/articles/10/pdfs/do-migrants-take-the-jobs-of-native-workers.pdf?v=1) between George Washington University and IZA Germany found that "Neither public opinion nor evidence-based research supports the claim of some politicians and the media that immigrants take the jobs of native-born workers."
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3.2.1. Con: The author of the paper is actually the creator of the Journal where it is published, [Amelie Constant](http://www.amelieconstant.com/AmelieConstant_March2017_Long_Web.pdf). According to her CV she has *always* published articles that portray immigration in a positive light in multiple countries. It is a peculiar position to be an advocate and a scholar.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3.2.2. Con: [iza.org](http://iza.org) and [glabor.org](https://glabor.org) are two organizations [administered](http://scholar.google.com/citations?user=9-mNytAAAAAJ&hl=en) by individuals - K F Zimmermann and Amelie F Constant - with interest on immigration and “open borders. They both have extensively worked with the [Central European University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_European_University) much focus of controversy as it is funded by George Soros. To be fair to Mr Zimmermann he also wrote a very neutral article on the [refugee issue](http://fortune.com/2015/11/10/europe-migrant-crisis-germany/)
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3.3. Con: Public [opinion](https://pdfs.semanticscholar.org/4f09/d9a71fd5942f171146fabc2d385a3960c364.pdf) and research show that immigrants compete with locals [lowering](https://scholar.google.com/scholar?start=10&q=immigrants+impact+on+the+economy+job&hl=es&scisbd=1&as_sdt=0,5#d=gs_qabs&p=&u=%23p%3DeTLHyOvu448J) both their [wages](http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/001979398704000305).
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3.3.1. Con: The [wages](http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/001979398704000305) report acknowledges that "The effects of shifts in immigrant supply on the earnings of native-born men are, however, very small", and that increased migrant population correlates directly with existing migrants wages decreasing \(10% more migrants correlates to 10% lower migrant wages\). This supports the idea that migrants mostly compete amongst themselves for some jobs, instead of replacing native workers.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3.3.2. Con: Public [opinion](https://pdfs.semanticscholar.org/4f09/d9a71fd5942f171146fabc2d385a3960c364.pdf) in South Korea is unlikely to be representative of the global picture, because of [Koreas history of Nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_nationalism). The paper itself suggests that "South Korea is a country where deep-seated nationalistic sentiments have been forged by an alleged ethnic and cultural homogeneity". A nationalistic country is likely to have a lower public opinion of migration.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3.3.2.1. Con: European nations have a history of nationalism. In fact most nations have had a history of nationalism.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.5.3.4. Con: If immigrants did not arrive to do these jobs, they would quickly become less low-paid, by the laws of supply and demand.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6. Pro: The moral reputation of high-income nations will benefit by taking in refugees.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1. Pro: There are already several countries that take in many more refugees than the first world countries do, making first world countries look bad. First world countries wouldn't look as bad if they took in more refugees.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1.1. Con: The attention that poor countries receive for their efforts at taking in refugees is small. High-income countries do not even have to compete with them to attract positive attention for their own efforts.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1.2. Pro: Poorer countries host most [refugees](http://www.unhcr.org/news/latest/2017/2/58b001ab4/poorer-countries-host-forcibly-displaced-report-shows.html).
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1.2.1. Pro: Poor countries host refugees in [poor conditions](https://sites.google.com/site/absentafghans/life-within-refugee-camps) because they have a shortage of finances and corrupt governments. High income countries can give refugees better lives, health and education, therefore providing a better standard of living.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1.2.2. Pro: The top nations taking in refugees from the Syrian Civil War have in fact not been [high-income nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_Civil_War).
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1.3. Pro: The first world countries which took in many refugees \(for example, Germany and Austria\) were [applauded for it](http://www.unhcr.org/news/latest/2015/9/55eae4116/unhcr-applauds-austria-germany-refugees-march-across-hungary.html).
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1.3.1. Con: Sweden has received a negative image recently both nationally and internationally because of its large influx of refugees.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1.3.1.1. Pro: The Swedish anti-immigration party, [the Sweden Democrats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweden_Democrats), has gone from below 4% in the 2006 election to 13% in the 2014 election and having 18% support in 2017 according to [polls](https://www.thelocal.se/20170601/anti-immigration-sweden-democrats-overtake-moderates-as-swedens-second-largest-party-poll), making them the 2nd biggest party in Swedish politics.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1.3.1.2. Pro: Misleading [claims](https://www.gatestoneinstitute.org/6697/sweden-collapse) that Sweden cannot [handle](https://www.nytimes.com/2015/11/14/opinion/swedens-self-inflicted-nightmare.html) the large influx of refugees and that it is becoming [dangerous](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2017/02/25/who-is-nils-bildt-swedish-national-security-advisor-interviewed-by-fox-news-is-a-mystery-to-swedes/?utm_term=.cf18c2973c21) to live in has been spread in the US and even received national coverage.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.1.3.1.2.1. Pro: A [report](http://www.government.se/articles/2017/02/facts-about-migration-and-crime-in-sweden/) released by the Swedish government shows that contrary to these claims, Sweden is currently stable, safe and economically strong.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.2. Con: Enhancing moral reputation this way can be seen as a sham device to improve public image, therefore causing countries to be in a worse position than before.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.2.1. Pro: There [exists](https://www.rt.com/politics/230559-russia-west-attitude-poll/) a strong anti-Western sentiment in places like Russia and the Middle East. Attempts by Western countries to act positively can be seen as hostile and concealing an insidious motive.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.2.1.1. Pro: Foreign aid, which presumably is for helping allies, is often [seen as](https://www.israelrising.com/foreign-aid-form-neo-colonialism/) a form of neocolonialism which is used to establish control over a country by creating a relationship of dependence.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.2.1.2. Pro: Western policies in the Middle East and South Asia [conflict](https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1007/978-1-349-00637-3_14) with the resurgence of nationalism in these areas. Western interference, although it may be helpful, is seen as a threat to local autonomy and control.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.2.1.3. Con: Strongly anti-Western countries will fabricate anti-Western narratives out of anything the West does. Accepting refugees will not lead to any worsening in anti-Western narratives.
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.2.1.3.1. Pro: There is [footage](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TrS0uNBuG9c) of a North Korean museum dedicated to war crimes perpetrated by US American troops, which seem exaggerated and possibly unbelievable to Westeners. \(Linked video may not be available in all geographic locations.\)
1.1.6.5.3.1.1.6.3. Con: It is unclear what benefit an enhanced moral reputation actually brings to a state. As such, high income countries should prioritise other concerns.
