This would also ensures a high-income country isn't building an affordable working class at the expense of a lower-income country.
1.13.1.5. Con: Refugees who are able to start anew, make a living, work a job or even receive training and an education in high-income countries are worth much more once they return home than refugees who spend years in limbo and in camps.
1.13.1.5.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.6.5.1.4.11.
1.13.1.6. Pro: Taking in refugees is by definition removing dissenters from authoritarian or war-filled areas. Removing dissenters increases proportionally the number of regime loyalists. Making democratization and the improvement of the situation less likely. In short, taking in refugees might doom those areas to an authoritarian future.
1.13.1.6.1. Con: Most refugees cannot be said to be of significant political relevance in their home countries.
1.13.1.6.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.4.6.9.1.2.1.
1.13.1.6.2. Con: Most contemporary conflicts that result in refugee movements could hardly be solved through a larger number of government opponents.
1.13.1.6.2.1. Pro: The conflict in Afghanistan is driven by dissenters: the Taliban trying to oust the country's government for the purpose of imposing their own religious and political structures.
1.13.1.6.2.2. Pro: The civil war in Syria is propelled by dissenters from various directions, including ISIS, Kurdish forces, numerous other extremist groups and various foreign powers, most of which don't agree with each other.
1.13.1.6.2.3. Pro: The source of Somalia's instability has for decades been the weakness of its governments that have been besieged by various dissident forces.
1.13.1.7. Pro: -> See 1.6.10.1.2.1.
1.13.1.8. Con: That harm is entirely acceptable in order to do a good deed for the sake of goodness.
1.13.1.9. Pro: If high income countries have a standing policy to accept refugees, such a policy could subsidize a certain kind of immigration over another. Despotic leaders may be more violent towards their own people if they know that a certain segment \(i.e. different religious sect\) of the population will be able to flee more easily.
1.13.1.9.1. Pro: People in distress get priority over all others who want to immigrate, which in turn encourages distress.
1.13.1.10. Con: In their home countries, refugees can be a burden \(for reasons of scarcity \(water, food, work, ...\) or political, social, cultural unrest\). If more people leave their country, this can reduce the strain and help it recover faster.
1.13.1.11. Con: If high-income countries do not accept refugees, then those refugees will most likely end up stuck in a refugee camp, not back in their home country.
1.13.2. Pro: France is reacting to people taking "crazy risks" by planning to establish so-called ["hotspots"](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-40738199) in Libya to prevent people who would not be eligible for asylum from risking their lives crossing the sea.
1.13.2.1. Con: The first "hotspot" established on the Greek island of Lesvos [did not have any impact](http://www.spiegel.de/international/europe/problems-with-migrant-registration-centers-in-greece-a-1074372.html) on the flow of refugees.
1.13.3. Pro: [Germany's open-door policy](https://theweek.com/articles/669030/angela-merkel-destroying-europe) in 2015 may have encouraged many more refugees to risk the journey to Europe.
1.13.3.1. Con: If an open door policy encourages refugees to take the risk of travel, it is only because the risk of not traveling is even greater. Therefore, you reduce the total risk to these people, by giving them the option to travel. A risky option can still be safer than a riskier option.
1.13.3.2. Pro: The awareness that this means there is a good chance of being accepted into Germany as a refugee, which is a safer environment than the refugee camps close to the place where the refugees are fleeing from, creates an additional incentive to risk the journey.
1.13.3.3. Pro: This policy caused [problems](https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/europe-struggles-to-handle-accelerating-flow-of-refugees/2015/09/07/e2bbc509-414b-4890-bedf-c76b37ae109a_story.html?utm_term=.98345261271e) with transportation and support in Greece and along the Balkan route as refugees tried to get to Germany.
1.13.3.4. Con: There is no reason to conclude that Germany's open door policy caused these refugees to attempt to reach Europe. It is most likely that they would have attempted the journey anyways due to worsening conditions in their home countries.
1.13.3.4.1. Con: [Bill Gates](https://www.rt.com/news/395356-migrants-overwhelm-europe-gates/) suggested that European leaders' generosity motivates people to migrate to Europe, and that this will overwhelm European countries like Germany.
1.13.3.4.1.1. Con: In a country like Germany with a population of more than 80 million people, less then a million refugees can't be considered to "overwhelm" the country
1.13.3.4.1.2. Con: Bill Gates is not an expert on migration. His opinions should not be considered relevant on this topic.
1.13.3.4.1.3. Pro: Through his [foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_%26_Melinda_Gates_Foundation), Gates has been involved with battling poverty and its underlying reasons for many years. We can assume he has some insight into issues of migration and displacement.
1.13.3.4.1.4. Con: It is not clear at all that Bill Gates is arguing this. There are clear statements from his own [website](https://www.gatesnotes.com/About-Bill-Gates/A-Conversation-with-Bill-Gates-How-Can-Countries-Help) that say migration is a good thing. There are no references to this quote from Bill Gates himself. I don't know how relevant it is that the media that have primarily circulated this claim are all closely affiliated with the right wing or known to have anti-immigration sentiments.
1.13.3.4.1.5. Con: Gates's statement is anecdotal, and there is no concrete evidence for his suggestion.
1.13.4. Con: Organizing safe passage for refugees would mitigate the risks.
1.13.4.1. Con: Organizing safe passage for refugees is a political impossibility as the prospect of ever more refugees would provoke ardent opposition in most high-income countries.
1.13.4.2. Con: If safety was the most important reason then closer countries would be preferred rather than those that have higher income.
1.13.4.3. Pro: Granting refugees [safe passage](http://www.doctorswithoutborders.org/article/people-are-not-numbers-refugees-need-safe-passage) would fight human trafficking and human smuggling, since refugees would no longer need to travel by illegal routes, and safe mechanisms of transportation could be organised for them.
1.13.4.4. Con: There are [too many](http://www.unhcr.org/figures-at-a-glance.html) refugees to provide safe passage for them all. It would involve huge fiscal investments to streamline international travel on such a large scale.
1.13.5. Con: If people are willing to take huge risks in order to seek asylum, this indicates that the situations they are leaving are very bad indeed. This strengthens the imperative to take in refugees, rather than reducing it.
1.13.5.1. Con: That is only partly true. Either the situation they are leaving is bad, or the incentives for arriving are great. Information from charities on the ground in Iraq indicate that the [smugglers](http://dan-drapal.cz/index.php/cz/politicke-clanky/333-zpravy-a-dojmy-z-erbilu) are promising would-be refugees to receive free housing and guaranteed monthly income of €1000 upon arrival to Germany.
1.13.5.2. Con: Refugees may be unaware of the degree of risk associated with attempting to cross the Mediterranean, which has [increased massively](http://www.pbs.org/wgbh/frontline/article/for-those-crossing-the-mediterranean-a-higher-risk-of-death/) lately.
1.13.5.2.1. Con: Often information and advice is given on [social media](http://news.sky.com/story/refugees-use-social-media-as-journey-guide-10347981) from refugees who have made the journey to those making the trip.
1.13.5.2.1.1. Con: That does not mean that desperate people know what to trust or that they even have access to such information.
1.13.5.3. Pro: It is wise to treat refugees as informed rational agents.  News of tragedies are well publicized throughout Europe and the countries refugees are leaving.  Because only refugees can know the specifics of their situation and needs, only they can be informed enough to decide which option is best for them.
1.13.6. Con: Refusing to accept refugees necessitates closing down travel routes to prevent refugees amassing at the borders of high-income countries. This leads to people taking [more risks](https://theconversation.com/european-policy-is-driving-refugees-to-more-dangerous-routes-across-the-med-56625), and subsequently, to more people dying on their journey to high income countries.
1.13.6.1. Con: While some may take more risks and use alternate routes to enter countries there is no evidence offered as to what share choose to do this. Many prospective migrants may choose to stay in their countries. This will be especially true if migrants believe that they are likely to be deported even if they arrive in the country.
1.13.6.2. Pro: Now that the Balkan route is closing refugees are desperate enough to consider [crossing](http://www.newsweek.com/europe-refugee-crisis-libya-italy-central-mediterranean-446528) the sea to Italy in order to reach the EU. This crossing is considered the "most dangerous" route, yet thousands risk their lives hoping to escape poverty and being able to send money to their families.
1.13.6.2.1. Pro: Reporters [uncovered](https://edition.cnn.com/2017/11/14/africa/libya-migrant-auctions/) an active slave trade in Libya, one of the countries on the route to Italy. There, refugees are sold as workers.
1.13.6.2.1.1. Pro: This is directly related to the authorities' actions: Fewer ships can leave the Libyan coast due to increased surveillance, so smugglers cannot move refugees and instead sell them.
1.13.7. Pro: Smugglers exploit refugees attempting to cross the Mediterranean and subject them to horrific risks.
1.13.7.1. Con: For many refugees the risk of short-term exploitation by smugglers has to be balanced against the long-term life-threatening risk of staying.
1.13.7.2. Pro: [Many minors](https://www.theguardian.com/global-development/2017/may/17/traffickers-smugglers-exploit-record-rise-unaccompanied-child-refugees-migrants-unicef-report) who attempt to reach Europe alone are instead forced into slavery or prostitution.
1.13.7.3. Pro: Migrants often end up suffocating in transport containers or drowning on unsafe boats because of the [neglect of smugglers](https://www.unodc.org/toc/en/crimes/migrant-smuggling.html).
1.13.7.4. Con: -> See 1.13.4.3.
1.13.8. Con: Accepting refugees would provide them with a legal avenue into countries. This means they would not have to pay smugglers to attempt to smuggle them into Europe through risky routes.
1.13.8.1. Con: Many refugees would still use the services of smugglers in order to not get stuck in Turkey or European border countries and to claim asylum in a country of their choosing.
1.13.8.1.1. Pro: Of the refugees who applied for asylum in Europe in 2016, [almost half](http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/index.php/Asylum_quarterly_report) did so in either Germany, France or the UK, the preferred countries of many refugees.
1.13.9. Pro: -> See 1.13.5.2.
1.13.10. Con: Complications of attempts to fulfill moral duty do not negate moral duty.
1.13.10.1. Con: If the attempt to fulfill the duty to help refugees motivates them to engage in a journey that endangers many of them, this runs clearly counter to this moral duty in the first place.
1.13.10.2. Pro: If there is a moral duty to accept refugees, that will not be negated by a pragmatic problem like this which has solutions. If there are reasonable ways to mitigate the related danger, the obligation in question should extend to discharging those ways.
1.13.10.3. Con: Moral duty is relative to the sensitivity of a specific society. Moreover the first moral duty of a state is the well-being of its citizens.
1.13.10.4. Pro: By way of example: high-income nations can allow for refugees to make rational decisions by spreading information about risk. Once they do so, the obligation to take in refugees would extend to whoever makes the journey.
1.13.10.5. Pro: -> See 1.13.4.
